          &lt;a expr:class='data:post.oldLinkClass' expr:href='data:post.olderLinkUrl'&gt;
            &lt;data:post.olderLinkText/&gt;
          &lt;/a&gt;
          &amp;#160;
          &lt;data:post.commentRangeText/&gt;
          &amp;#160;
          &lt;a expr:class='data:post.newLinkClass' expr:href='data:post.newerLinkUrl'&gt;
            &lt;data:post.newerLinkText/&gt;
          &lt;/a&gt;
          &lt;a expr:class='data:post.newLinkClass' expr:href='data:post.newestLinkUrl'&gt;
            &lt;data:post.newestLinkText/&gt;
          &lt;/a&gt;
        &lt;/span&gt;
      &lt;/b:if&gt;

      &lt;p class='comment-footer'&gt;
        &lt;b:if cond='data:post.embedCommentForm'&gt;
          &lt;b:if cond='data:post.allowNewComments'&gt;
            &lt;b:include data='post' name='comment-form'/&gt;
          &lt;b:else/&gt;
            &lt;data:post.noNewCommentsText/&gt;
          &lt;/b:if&gt;
        &lt;b:elseif cond='data:post.allowComments'/&gt;
          &lt;a expr:href='data:post.addCommentUrl' expr:onclick='data:post.addCommentOnclick'&gt;&lt;data:postCommentMsg/&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
        &lt;/b:if&gt;
      &lt;/p&gt;
    &lt;/b:if&gt;
    &lt;b:if cond='data:showCmtPopup'&gt;
      &lt;div id='comment-popup'&gt;
        &lt;iframe allowtransparency='true' frameborder='0' id='comment-actions' name='comment-actions' scrolling='no'&gt;
        &lt;/iframe&gt;
      &lt;/div&gt;
    &lt;/b:if&gt;

id='comment-editor-src'/\> \<iframe allowtransparency='true'
class='blogger-iframe-colorize blogger-comment-from-post'
expr:height='data:cmtIframeInitialHeight' frameborder='0'
id='comment-editor' name='comment-editor' src='' width='100%'/\>
\</b:if\> \<data:post.cmtfpIframe/\> \<script type='text/javascript'\>
BLOG_CMT_createIframe(&#39;\<data:post.appRpcRelayPath/\>&#39;);
\</script\> \</div\> \</b:includable\> \<b:includable
id='threaded_comment_js' var='post'\> \<script async='async'
expr:src='data:post.commentSrc' type='text/javascript'/\>

\<script type='text/javascript'\> (function() { var items =
\<data:post.commentJso/\>; var msgs = \<data:post.commentMsgs/\>; var
config = \<data:post.commentConfig/\>;

// \<!\[CDATA\[ var cursor = null; if (items && items.length \> 0) {
cursor = parseInt(items\[items.length - 1\].timestamp) + 1; }

      var bodyFromEntry = function(entry) {
        var text = (entry &amp;&amp;
                    ((entry.content &amp;&amp; entry.content.$t) ||
                     (entry.summary &amp;&amp; entry.summary.$t))) ||
            '';
        if (entry &amp;&amp; entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
          for (var k in entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
            if (entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].name == 'blogger.contentRemoved') {
              return '&lt;span class="deleted-comment"&gt;' + text + '&lt;/span&gt;';
            }
          }
        }
        return text;
      }

      var parse = function(data) {
        cursor = null;
        var comments = [];
        if (data &amp;&amp; data.feed &amp;&amp; data.feed.entry) {
          for (var i = 0, entry; entry = data.feed.entry[i]; i++) {
            var comment = {};
            // comment ID, parsed out of the original id format
            var id = /blog-(\d+).post-(\d+)/.exec(entry.id.$t);
            comment.id = id ? id[2] : null;
            comment.body = bodyFromEntry(entry);
            comment.timestamp = Date.parse(entry.published.$t) + '';
            if (entry.author &amp;&amp; entry.author.constructor === Array) {
              var auth = entry.author[0];
              if (auth) {
                comment.author = {
                  name: (auth.name ? auth.name.$t : undefined),
                  profileUrl: (auth.uri ? auth.uri.$t : undefined),
                  avatarUrl: (auth.gd$image ? auth.gd$image.src : undefined)
                };
              }
            }
            if (entry.link) {
              if (entry.link[2]) {
                comment.link = comment.permalink = entry.link[2].href;
              }
              if (entry.link[3]) {
                var pid = /.*comments\/default\/(\d+)\?.*/.exec(entry.link[3].href);
                if (pid &amp;&amp; pid[1]) {
                  comment.parentId = pid[1];
                }
              }
            }
            comment.deleteclass = 'item-control blog-admin';
            if (entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
              for (var k in entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
                if (entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].name == 'blogger.itemClass') {
                  comment.deleteclass += ' ' + entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].value;
                } else if (entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].name == 'blogger.displayTime') {
                  comment.displayTime = entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].value;
                }
              }
            }
            comments.push(comment);
          }
        }
        return comments;
      };

      var paginator = function(callback) {
        if (hasMore()) {
          var url = config.feed + '?alt=json&amp;v=2&amp;orderby=published&amp;reverse=false&amp;max-results=50';
          if (cursor) {
            url += '&amp;published-min=' + new Date(cursor).toISOString();
          }
          window.bloggercomments = function(data) {
            var parsed = parse(data);
            cursor = parsed.length &lt; 50 ? null
                : parseInt(parsed[parsed.length - 1].timestamp) + 1
            callback(parsed);
            window.bloggercomments = null;
          }
          url += '&amp;callback=bloggercomments';
          var script = document.createElement('script');
          script.type = 'text/javascript';
          script.src = url;
          document.getElementsByTagName('head')[0].appendChild(script);
        }
      };
      var hasMore = function() {
        return !!cursor;
      };
      var getMeta = function(key, comment) {
        if ('iswriter' == key) {
          var matches = !!comment.author
              &amp;&amp; comment.author.name == config.authorName
              &amp;&amp; comment.author.profileUrl == config.authorUrl;
          return matches ? 'true' : '';
        } else if ('deletelink' == key) {
          return config.baseUri + '/delete-comment.g?blogID='
               + config.blogId + '&amp;postID=' + comment.id;
        } else if ('deleteclass' == key) {
          return comment.deleteclass;
        }
        return '';
      };

      var replybox = null;
      var replyUrlParts = null;
      var replyParent = undefined;

      var onReply = function(commentId, domId) {
        if (replybox == null) {
          // lazily cache replybox, and adjust to suit this style:
          replybox = document.getElementById('comment-editor');
          if (replybox != null) {
            replybox.height = '250px';
            replybox.style.display = 'block';
            replyUrlParts = replybox.src.split('#');
          }
        }
        if (replybox &amp;&amp; (commentId !== replyParent)) {
          replybox.src = '';
          document.getElementById(domId).insertBefore(replybox, null);
          replybox.src = replyUrlParts[0]
              + (commentId ? '&amp;parentID=' + commentId : '')
              + '#' + replyUrlParts[1];
          replyParent = commentId;
        }
      };

      var hash = (window.location.hash || '#').substring(1);
      var startThread, targetComment;
      if (/^comment-form_/.test(hash)) {
        startThread = hash.substring('comment-form_'.length);
      } else if (/^c[0-9]+$/.test(hash)) {
        targetComment = hash.substring(1);
      }

      // Configure commenting API:
      var configJso = {
        'maxDepth': config.maxThreadDepth
      };
      var provider = {
        'id': config.postId,
        'data': items,
        'loadNext': paginator,
        'hasMore': hasMore,
        'getMeta': getMeta,
        'onReply': onReply,
        'rendered': true,
        'initComment': targetComment,
        'initReplyThread': startThread,
        'config': configJso,
        'messages': msgs
      };

      var render = function() {
        if (window.goog &amp;&amp; window.goog.comments) {
          var holder = document.getElementById('comment-holder');
          window.goog.comments.render(holder, provider);
        }
      };

      // render now, or queue to render when library loads:
      if (window.goog &amp;&amp; window.goog.comments) {
        render();
      } else {
        window.goog = window.goog || {};
        window.goog.comments = window.goog.comments || {};
        window.goog.comments.loadQueue = window.goog.comments.loadQueue || [];
        window.goog.comments.loadQueue.push(render);
      }
    })();

\</b:loop\> \</ul\> \<b:else/\> \<b:loop values='data:labels'

data:label.cssSize'\> \<b:if cond='data:blog.url == data:label.url'\>
\<span
expr:dir='data:blog.languageDirection'\>\<data:label.name/\>\</span\>
\<b:else/\> \<a expr:dir='data:blog.languageDirection'

Zextras Carbonio CE : Customize Printview/printpage Carbonio Comunity
Edition
```{=html}
</title>
```
`<content type='html'>`{=html}\<p\>&nbsp;\</p\>\<h2 data-pm-slice="1 3
\[\]"\>\<span style="font-family: georgia;"\>Cari Fail yang Mengandungi
Title "Carbonio"\</span\>\</h2\>\<ol data-spread="true"
start="1"\>\<li\>\<p\>\<span style="font-family: georgia;"\>Jalankan
arahan berikut untuk mencari fail yang mengandungi
"Carbonio":\</span\>\</p\>\<pre\>\<code\>grep
"&lt;title&gt;Carbonio&lt;/title&gt;"
/opt/zextras/web/iris/carbonio-mails-ui/\*
-rl\</code\>\</pre\>\</li\>\<li\>\<p\>\<span style="font-family:
georgia;"\>Arahan ini akan memaparkan senarai fail yang mengandungi teks
tersebut. Contoh yang saya
dapat:\</span\>\</p\>\<pre\>\<code\>/opt/zextras/web/iris/carbonio-mails-ui/30ed9d1491400e80f4ec5e16939456d00a4f3ce3/534.a41dc3b1.chunk.js
/opt/zextras/web/iris/carbonio-mails-ui/30ed9d1491400e80f4ec5e16939456d00a4f3ce3/534.a43dc6b1.chunk.map\</code\>\</pre\>\</li\>\</ol\>\<h2\>\<span
style="font-family: georgia;"\>Backup Fail\</span\>\</h2\>\<p\>\<span
style="font-family: georgia;"\>Dinasihatkan sentiasa buat salinan fail
sebelum melakukan sebarang perubahan.\</span\>\</p\>\<ol
data-spread="false" start="1"\>\<li\>\<p\>\<span style="font-family:
georgia;"\>Jalankan arahan berikut untuk membuat salinan
fail:\</span\>\</p\>\<pre\>\<code\>cp
/opt/zextras/web/iris/carbonio-mails-ui/30ed9d1491400e80f4ec5e16939456d00a4f3ce3/534.a41dc3b1.chunk.js
\</code\>/opt/zextras/web/iris/carbonio-mails-ui/30ed9d1491400e80f4ec5e16939456d00a4f3ce3/534.a41dc3b1.chunk.js.bak\</pre\>\</li\>\</ol\>\<h2\>\<span
style="font-family: georgia;"\>Menukar Title Menggunakan
\<code\>sed\</code\>\</span\>\</h2\>\<ol data-spread="false"
start="1"\>\<li\>\<p\>\<span style="font-family: georgia;"\>Gantikan
title "Carbonio" dengan tajuk baru menggunakan arahan
\<code\>sed\</code\>:\</span\>\</p\>\<pre\>\<code\>sed -i
s/"&lt;title&gt;Carbonio&lt;/title&gt;"/"&lt;title&gt;TAJUK
BARU&lt;/title&gt;"/g /opt/zextras/web/iris/carbonio-mails-ui/
30ed9d1491400e80f4ec5e16939456d00a4f3ce3/534.a41dc3b1.chunk.js\</code\>\</pre\>\<ul
data-spread="false"\>\<li\>\<p\>\<span style="font-family:
georgia;"\>Gantikan \<code\>TAJUK BARU\</code\> dengan teks yang anda
mahu.\</span\>\</p\>\</li\>\</ul\>\</li\>\</ol\>\<h2\>\<span
style="font-family: georgia;"\>Mengedit Secara
Manual&nbsp;\</span\>\</h2\>\<p\>\<span style="font-family:
georgia;"\>Sekiranya anda ingin mengedit fail secara manual, kena
berhati-hati:\</span\>\</p\>\<ol data-spread="false"
start="1"\>\<li\>\<p\>\<span style="font-family: georgia;"\>Buka fail
menggunakan editor teks seperti
\<code\>nano\</code\>:\</span\>\</p\>\<pre\>\<code\>nano
/opt/zextras/web/iris/carbonio-mails-ui/30ed9d1491400e80f4ec5e16939456d00a4f3ce3/534.a41dc3b1.chunk.js\</code\>\</pre\>\</li\>\<li\>\<p\>\<span
style="font-family: georgia;"\>Cari baris yang
mengandungi:\</span\>\</p\>\<pre\>\<code\>&lt;title&gt;Carbonio&lt;/title&gt;\</code\>\</pre\>\</li\>\<li\>\<p\>\<span
style="font-family: georgia;"\>Tukar
kepada:\</span\>\</p\>\<pre\>\<code\>&lt;title&gt;TAJUK
BARU&lt;/title&gt;\</code\>\</pre\>\</li\>\<li\>\<p\>\<span
style="font-family: georgia;"\>Simpan fail dan keluar dari editor teks.
Kita juga boleh menukar Header Content dalam printview pada fail
ini.\</span\>\</p\>\</li\>\</ol\>`</content>`{=html}`<link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://lonurhazve.blogspot.com/feeds/8102702413987127760/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/>`{=html}`<link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://lonurhazve.blogspot.com/2025/01/zextras-carbonio-ce-customize.html#comment-form' title='0 Comments'/>`{=html}`<link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/8102702413987127760'/>`{=html}`<link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/8102702413987127760'/>`{=html}`<link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='https://lonurhazve.blogspot.com/2025/01/zextras-carbonio-ce-customize.html' title='Zextras Carbonio CE : Customize Printview/printpage Carbonio Comunity Edition'/>`{=html}`<author>`{=html}`<name>`{=html}lonurhazve`</name>`{=html}`<uri>`{=html}https://www.blogger.com/profile/16306879527733710247`</uri>`{=html}`<email>`{=html}noreply@blogger.com`</email>`{=html}`<gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='35' height='35' src='//www.blogger.com/img/blogger_logo_round_35.png'/>`{=html}`</author>`{=html}`<thr:total>`{=html}0`</thr:total>`{=html}`</entry>`{=html}`<entry>`{=html}`<id>`{=html}tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-702950587710156521.post-4277876058921568646`</id>`{=html}`<published>`{=html}2017-04-21T11:55:00.001+08:00`</published>`{=html}`<updated>`{=html}2017-04-21T11:55:26.288+08:00`</updated>`{=html}`<app:control xmlns:app='http://purl.org/atom/app#'>`{=html}`<app:draft>`{=html}yes`</app:draft>`{=html}`</app:control>`{=html}`<category scheme='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#kind' term='http://schemas.google.com/blogger/2008/kind#post'/>`{=html}

Installation Owncloud
```{=html}
</title>
```
`<content type='html'>`{=html}\<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\> \<br
/\> Install Webserver dan MariaDB\<br /\> \<br /\> \<b\>#apt install
apache2 mariadb-server php7.0 php7.0-common libapache2-mod-php7.0
php7.0-gd php-xml-parser php7.0-json php7.0-curl php7.0-bz2 php7.0-zip
php7.0-mcrypt php7.0-mysql php7.0-mbstring memcached php-memcached
php-redis redis-server\</b\>\<br /\> \<b\>\<br /\>\</b\> \<b\>\<br
/\>\</b\> \<b\>Konfigurasi webserver\</b\>\<br /\> \<b\>\<br /\>\</b\>
Pastikan index.php berada di hadapan sekali dalam file dir.conf.\<br /\>
\<br /\> #vi /etc/apache2/mods-enabled/dir.conf\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<b\>---------------------------------------dir.conf-------------------------------------------------------------------------\</b\>\<br
/\> \<b\>\<ifmodule mod_dir.c=""\>\</ifmodule\>\</b\>\<br /\>
\<b\>&nbsp; &nbsp; DirectoryIndex index.php index.html\</b\>\<br /\>
\<b\>\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\> \<b\>Meningkatkan
performance apache webserver&nbsp;\</b\>\<br /\> \<b\>\<br /\>\</b\>
Edit global configuration apache seper berikut :\<br /\> \<br /\>
#vi&nbsp;/etc/apache2/apache2.conf\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<b\>------------------------------------apache2.conf---------------------------------------------------------------------\</b\>\<br
/\> \<b\>Timeout 20\</b\>\<br /\> \<b\>KeepAliveTimeout 100\</b\>\<br
/\> \<b\>MaxKeepAliveRequests 200\</b\>\<br /\> \<b\>\<br /\>\</b\>
\<b\>\<br
/\>\</b\>`</content>`{=html}`<link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://lonurhazve.blogspot.com/2017/04/installation-owncloud.html#comment-form' title='0 Comments'/>`{=html}`<link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/4277876058921568646'/>`{=html}`<link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/4277876058921568646'/>`{=html}`<author>`{=html}`<name>`{=html}lonurhazve`</name>`{=html}`<uri>`{=html}https://www.blogger.com/profile/16306879527733710247`</uri>`{=html}`<email>`{=html}noreply@blogger.com`</email>`{=html}`<gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='35' height='35' src='//www.blogger.com/img/blogger_logo_round_35.png'/>`{=html}`</author>`{=html}`<thr:total>`{=html}0`</thr:total>`{=html}`</entry>`{=html}`<entry>`{=html}`<id>`{=html}tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-702950587710156521.post-3223663246524035846`</id>`{=html}`<published>`{=html}2015-09-29T16:19:00.005+08:00`</published>`{=html}`<updated>`{=html}2015-11-22T15:39:09.513+08:00`</updated>`{=html}`<category scheme='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#kind' term='http://schemas.google.com/blogger/2008/kind#post'/>`{=html}

Xenserver Tools For Your Virtual Machine
```{=html}
</title>
```
`<content type='html'>`{=html}\<br /\> \<br /\> \<div style="text-align:
justify;"\> Menggunakan VM yang opensource mungkin terdedah dengan
kerja-kerja yang banyak berbanding yang berlesen. Tapi terpulanglah
kepada kita, apabila nmemilih jalan yang mudah kita tidak akan mengecapi
pengalaman2 yang amat berharga sepanjang perjalanan tersebut.\</div\>
\<div style="text-align: justify;"\> \<br /\>\</div\> \<div
style="text-align: justify;"\> Xenserver kini versi 6.5 yang merupakan
opensource virtualization machine. Mempunyai kemudahan support yang
commercial tapi anda perlu keluarkan wang dan berikan arahan melalui
mulut anda semuanya akan jadi bukannya dengan command.\</div\> \<div
style="text-align: justify;"\> \<br /\>\</div\> \<div style="text-align:
justify;"\> Xenserver with xencenter and Equalogic Storage is good
Practices.\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\> \<br /\>\</div\>
\<div style="text-align: justify;"\> How Xenserver Tools For Your
Virtual Machine\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\> \<br
/\>\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\> Xenserver Tools
Installation Linux OS\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\> \<br
/\>\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\> Load from
Machine&nbsp;xs-tools.iso\<br /\> \<br /\> \<div class="separator"
style="clear: both; text-align: center;"\> \<a
href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEguZG-40L0rzabk1o7EUZKubmqrpBajloMeJwKsKQLsrbi7EpaGYJE38sQ3zP84tH6rBAiNCQEFPqxrg2dho40qq-mwDOqs6V5vn9-Aauo9hNp9jKUDc_jrd9Y34p_pZcFp5zGSraUbZw/s1600/xs-tools1.jpg"
imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"\>\<img

src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEguZG-40L0rzabk1o7EUZKubmqrpBajloMeJwKsKQLsrbi7EpaGYJE38sQ3zP84tH6rBAiNCQEFPqxrg2dho40qq-mwDOqs6V5vn9-Aauo9hNp9jKUDc_jrd9Y34p_pZcFp5zGSraUbZw/s1600/xs-tools1.jpg"
/\>\</a\>\</div\> \<br /\>\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\>

\<b\>#sudo mount /dev/cdrom /tmp\</b\>\</div\> \<div style="text-align:
justify;"\> \<b\>\<br /\>\</b\>\</div\> \<div style="text-align:

confirmation\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\> \<br

style="text-align: justify;"\> Umount back\</div\> \<div

imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"\>\<img

`<content type='html'>`{=html}`</content>`{=html}`<link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/7935523797852116613'/>`{=html}`<link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/7935523797852116613'/>`{=html}`<author>`{=html}`<name>`{=html}lonurhazve`</name>`{=html}`<uri>`{=html}https://www.blogger.com/profile/16306879527733710247`</uri>`{=html}`<email>`{=html}noreply@blogger.com`</email>`{=html}`<gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='35' height='35' src='//www.blogger.com/img/blogger_logo_round_35.png'/>`{=html}`</author>`{=html}`<thr:total>`{=html}0`</thr:total>`{=html}`</entry>`{=html}`<entry>`{=html}`<id>`{=html}tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-702950587710156521.post-7631698355092997307`</id>`{=html}`<published>`{=html}2014-04-29T07:23:00.000+08:00`</published>`{=html}`<updated>`{=html}2014-04-29T07:23:32.680+08:00`</updated>`{=html}`<app:control xmlns:app='http://purl.org/atom/app#'>`{=html}`<app:draft>`{=html}yes`</app:draft>`{=html}`</app:control>`{=html}`<category scheme='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#kind' term='http://schemas.google.com/blogger/2008/kind#post'/>`{=html}

`<content type='html'>`{=html}Tambah User Dan Home Dir\<br /\>
\<b\>adduser newuser --home /var/users/newuser\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\>
ModSecurity\<br /\> \<div class="postbody"\> \<div class="postrow"\>
\<h2 class="posttitle icon"\>
http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2219109 \</h2\> \<h2
class="posttitle icon"\> Installing and Configuring ModSecurity \</h2\>
\<div class="content"\> \<div id="post_message_12998685"\> \<blockquote
class="postcontent restore"\> If you're like me, the idea of running
your own web server is both appealing and a bit scary. I love the idea
of hosting blogs and on-line gaming for my friends, family and other
guests but as with many things, the bad guys are more than happy to drop
a giant turd into the punch bowl. There always has been and always will
be a percentage of the world's population that are jerks. No matter what
you present to the world, no matter how good, this group of people can
be counted on to try to spoil it in order to enrich themselves or out of
a simple mean-spirited nature. This is where ModSecurity is your
friend.\<br /\> \<br /\> In order for ModSecuity to help you it must be
properly installed, configured and rules must be added and activated. A
mistake in any of these steps can, at best, stop your web server from
running or at worse, allow your web server to run while at the same time
giving you a false sense of security. Also as new exploits are
discovered the rules should be updated so that these exploits fail.\<br
/\> \<br /\> I will try to walk you through the process step by step but
I am no expert in this area so please if you have information to
contribute please do so.\<br /\> \<br /\> This article assumes that you
have LAMP installed which includes a working web server. I have found
that unlike the articles about ModSecurity already on the Internet, the
articles dealing with the installation and configuration of LAMP are
adequate. If you need help you can find it \<a
href="https://help.ubuntu.com/community/ApacheMySQLPHP"
target="\_blank"\>here\</a\>. However, the current package used by
Ubuntu 14.04 to install ModSecurity has a number of differences that
make using older setup and configuration instructions useless or at
least not very helpful. \<br /\> \<br /\> In this article I will ask you
to type in commands in a terminal window. Hold down the Control and Alt
keys and press the "T" key. Note: I used the upper case "T" to make it
easier to read but you should not hold down the shift key. i.e. use
CNTL-ALT-lower case t.\<br /\> \<br /\> Enter the following into a
terminal:\<br /\> \<b\>sudo apt-get install
libapache2-modsecurity\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> We have just installed
ModSecurity and placed a default package of rules onto our system.\<br
/\> \<br /\> Now we need to place a modsecurity.conf configuration file
into the\<b\> /etc/modsecurity\</b\> directory. The configuration file
is complex but luckily the package comes with a recommended
configuration file that we can use as a starting point. Let's copy the
recommended file:\<br /\> \<b\>sudo cp
/etc/modsecurity/modsecurity.conf-recommended
/etc/modsecurity/modsecurity.conf\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> We'll make
changes to this file later but for now let's check the apache2 log
directory:\<br /\> \<b\>ls /var/log/apache2\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> You
should see three files: \<b\>access.log, error.log and
other_vhosts_access.log\</b\>. This is the same as before we installed
ModSecurity. Now let's restart the apache2 service and check this
directory again:\<br /\> \<br /\> \<b\>sudo service apache2
reload\</b\>\<br /\> \<b\>ls /var/log/apache2\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> You
should now see four files: \<b\>access.log, error.log, modsec_audit.log
and other_vhosts_access.log\</b\>.\<br /\> This is a good sign. A new
log called \<b\>modsec_audit.log\</b\> was created!\<br /\> \<br /\>
When modsecurity is installed it is configured to only detect threats
based on it's activated rules and as far as I know, none of its rules
are activated which makes the whole thing pretty useless. We must do
three things to get ModSecurity working:\<br /\> \<br /\> 1. Activate
the rules.\<br /\> 2. Change the value in modsecurity.conf called
SecRuleEngine from DetectionOnly to On.\<br /\> 3. Modify
/etc/apache2/mods-available/Security2.conf.\<br /\> \<br /\> You should
ensure that the rules are working properly prior to changing
SecRuleEngine from "DetectionOnly" to "On." A bad rule could block the
users on your entire network from being able to access important
services. This is what is known as a RBE or "resume building event" in
the I.T. sector. So please, after we're finished, run ModSecurity set
for DetectionOnly for a while and check your logs to determine if tweaks
are needed. If there is a rule blocking your entire network it may be
wise to deactivate that rule prior to switching the SecRuleEngine value
to "On." (Note: English grammar dictates that I place a period inside
the quotes but it is not part of the actual value. i.e. The value should
be "SecRuleEngine On" not "SecRuleEngine On." if you want it to
work.)\<br /\> \<br /\> Let's look into the modsecurity-crs
direcotry:\<br /\> \<br /\> \<b\>ls
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> You should see
several directories and a conf file. What we're interested in right now
are the directories \<b\>activated_rules, base_rules, experimental_rules
and optional_rules\</b\>.\<br /\> \<br /\> Activating a rule is a simple
task. You simply put symbolic link into the activated_rules directory
that points to the rule you wish to activate.\<br /\> \<br /\> We want
to activate all of the rules in the base_rules and optional_rules
directories so execute the following commands in a terminal:\<br /\>
\<br /\> \<b\>cd /usr/share/modsecurity-crs/base_rules\</b\>\<br /\>
\<b\>for f in \* ; do sudo ln -s
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/base_rules/$f /usr/share/modsecurity-crs/activated_rules/$f
; done\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> \<b\>cd
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/optional_rules\</b\>\<br /\> \<b\>for f in \*
; do sudo ln -s
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/optional_rules/$f /usr/share/modsecurity-crs/activated_rules/$f
; done\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> I tried activating the rules in
experimental_rules directory but got an error message when I restarted
apache2: \<b\>Could not open geo database
"/usr/share/GeoIP/GeoLiteCity.dat": No such file or directory\</b\>\<br
/\> \<br /\> I guess that's why they call it experimental. If you think
you might have better luck you can create the symlinks with the
following commands:\<br /\> \<br /\> \<i\>\<span style="color: red;"\>cd
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/experimental_rules\<br /\> for f in \* ; do
sudo ln -s
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/experimental_rules/$f /usr/share/modsecurity-crs/activated_rules/$f
; done\</span\>\</i\>\<br /\> \<br /\> Next we need to tell apache where
to find the activated rules. Open the
/etc/apache2/mods-available/security2.conf file.\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<b\>sudo nano /etc/apache2/mods-available/security2.conf\</b\>\<br /\>
\<br /\> At the end of the file just before \</blockquote\> \</div\>
\</div\> \</div\> \</div\> enter the following lines:\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<b\>Include "/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/*.conf"\<br /\> Include
"/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/activated_rules/*.conf"\</b\>\<br /\> \<br
/\> Please note that the order is important. If you switch them
ModSecurity will not block anything.\<br /\> \<br /\> The first line
includes a set of rules that was in the modsecurity-crs directory and
the second line tells appache where to find our symlinks .\<br /\> \<br
/\> Save the file by pressing CNTL-O. (Hold the control key and press
alpha O)\<br /\> Then exit with CNTL-X\<br /\> \<br /\> We must enable
the headers module, this allows ModSecurity to control and modify the
HTTP headers for both requests and responses.\<br /\> \<br /\> \<b\>sudo
a2enmod headers\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> Now restart apache:\<br /\>
\<b\>sudo service apache2 restart\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> ModSecurity
should now be running in detection mode. After you're sure it would not
be blocking legitimate traffic you should do the following:\<br /\> \<br
/\> \<b\>sudo nano /etc/modsecurity/modsecurity.conf\</b\>\<br /\> \<br
/\> Find this line:\<br /\> SecRuleEngine DetectionOnly\<br /\> \<br /\>
and change it to:\<br /\> \<br /\> SecRuleEngine On\<br /\> \<br /\> I
hope these instructions help! \<br /\>
\<b\>http://secure-ubuntu-server.blogspot.com/2013/02/howto-secure-apache-on-ubuntu-server.html
\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\>
http://unixbhaskar.wordpress.com/2012/01/26/mod_security-and-mod_evasive-implementation-and-testing-on-scientific-linux/\<br
/\> \<br /\> \<br /\>
&nbsp;http://paynedigital.com/articles/2011/09/setting-up-and-securing-a-phpmyadmin-install-on-ubuntu-10-04\<br
/\> \<h1\> Setting up and securing a phpMyAdmin install on Ubuntu
10.04\</h1\> \<div class="article-meta bump-out"\> \<div
class="article-meta\_\_published"\> \<time class="split-after"\>6th
September 2011\</time\>

            &lt;a href="http://paynedigital.com/articles/2011/09/setting-up-and-securing-a-phpmyadmin-install-on-ubuntu-10-04#comments"&gt;No comments&lt;/a&gt;
                            &lt;span class="split-before"&gt;Tags:&lt;/span&gt;
                                    &lt;a class="" href="http://paynedigital.com/articles/tag/apache"&gt;Apache&lt;/a&gt;,                                     &lt;a class="" href="http://paynedigital.com/articles/tag/mysql"&gt;MySQL&lt;/a&gt;,                                     &lt;a class="" href="http://paynedigital.com/articles/tag/php"&gt;PHP&lt;/a&gt;,                                     &lt;a class="" href="http://paynedigital.com/articles/tag/server%20administration"&gt;Server Administration&lt;/a&gt;                                    &lt;/div&gt;

\</div\> \<div class="article-content"\> Last time out we looked at
setting up a LAMP server ready to start developing dynamic websites,
without really going into much detail beyond the absolute basics. Day to
day web development on a LAMP stack by and large ignores the LA and
concentrates on the MP - so let's have a look at getting one of the more
common ways of accessing MySQL set up on a newly prepared server. Note
that the rest of this post assumes you have followed the instructions
found in the \<a
href="http://paynedigital.com/2011/08/preparing-a-new-lamp-server-on-rackspace-cloud"
title="Preparing a new LAMP server on Rackspace Cloud"\>LAMP server
setup post\</a\>.\<br /\> \<h2\> Installing phpMyAdmin\</h2\> Getting
phpMyAdmin installed is easy:\<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\>sudo apt-get
install phpmyadmin\</code\>\</pre\> This will ask you to install quite a
few dependent packages - go ahead and hit enter when prompted. The next
screen you'll see will be a package configuration prompt - go ahead and
select the option to configure phpMyAdmin for Apache2 automatically (use
space to select the option and then the arrow keys / tab to navigate to
\<b\>Ok\</b\>). You'll be returned to your terminal briefly before being
presented with another configuration screen.\<br /\> As per the
suggestion in the prompt, you should choose the default option which is
to let the installation process configure phpMyAdmin's own database,
which upon selection will prompt you for your database's administrative
user (aka root - though not your server's root account). Note that this
is a password you chose \<a
href="http://paynedigital.com/2011/08/preparing-a-new-lamp-server-on-rackspace-cloud"
title="Preparing a new LAMP server on Rackspace Cloud"\>during
setup\</a\>, not a new one you can just make up. The next prompt,
however, is a password for the (newly created) phpmyadmin user to access
its own database - simply enter a blank password and one will be
generated randomly. You should never need to login as this user, so it's
not a problem to not know what its password is.\<br /\> \<h2\> Accessing
phpMyAdmin\</h2\> Assuming the installation process above went smoothly,
you can now access your phpMyAdmin instance at:\<br /\>
\<pre\>\<code\>http://\<your-server-ip-address\>/phpmyadmin\</your-server-ip-address\>\</code\>\</pre\>
Great stuff - you're all set up to go. But if you're tempted to leave it
there, don't. Let's tighten up access a bit - after all, you've suddenly
exposed an easy access point to what will become a critically important
part of every site you host on this server. So what's the problem? Well,
there are two big ones.\<br /\> \<h2\> Problem #1\</h2\> First of all,
let's look at how the default configuration is exposing
\<code\>/phpmyadmin\</code\> to try and get a better understanding of
the out-of-the-box setup:\<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\>nick@pd01:\~\$ ls -lah
/etc/apache2/sites-enabled total 8.0K drwxr-xr-x 2 root root 4.0K
2011-09-06 09:35 . drwxr-xr-x 7 root root 4.0K 2011-09-06 09:35 ..
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 26 2011-09-06 09:35 000-default -&gt;
../sites-available/default \</code\>\</pre\> Hmm. Nothing to see there -
but that makes sense, since we didn't access it as a VirtualHost. Let's
try apache's conf.d directory:\<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\>nick@pd01:\~\$ ls
-lah /etc/apache2/conf.d/ total 20K drwxr-xr-x 2 root root 4.0K
2011-09-06 09:54 . drwxr-xr-x 7 root root 4.0K 2011-09-06 09:35 ..
-rw-r--r-- 1 root root 269 2010-04-13 20:20 charset lrwxrwxrwx 1 root
root 45 2011-09-06 09:43 javascript-common.conf -&gt;
/etc/javascript-common/javascript-common.conf -rw-r--r-- 1 root root
3.3K 2010-04-13 20:20 localized-error-pages lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 28
2011-09-06 09:54 phpmyadmin.conf -&gt; ../../phpmyadmin/apache.conf
-rw-r--r-- 1 root root 1.5K 2010-04-13 20:20 security\</code\>\</pre\>
Ah ha - so we've got a \<code\>phpmyadmin.conf\</code\> file which is
simply a symlink to \<code\>/etc/phpmyadmin/apache.conf\</code\>. That
makes sense. Let's take a look at the first few lines of it:\<br /\>
\<pre\>\<code\># phpMyAdmin default Apache configuration Alias
/phpmyadmin /usr/share/phpmyadmin \<directory phpmyadmin="" share=""
usr=""\> Options FollowSymLinks DirectoryIndex index.php \<ifmodule
mod_php5.c=""\> AddType application/x-httpd-php .php php_flag
magic_quotes_gpc Off php_flag track_vars On php_flag register_globals
Off php_value include_path . \</ifmodule\>
\</directory\>\</code\>\</pre\> That explains it then - we've simply got
a standard Apache Alias pointing every request starting with
\<code\>/phpmyadmin\</code\> to the phpMyAdmin installation
directory.\<br /\> \<h3\> So what?\</h3\> The problem is that the Alias
directive is applied globally. Assuming you're going to add multiple
VirtualHosts to this server, every single one of them will expose a
route to /phpmyadmin. If you set up a domain as per the \<a
href="http://paynedigital.com/2011/08/preparing-a-new-lamp-server-on-rackspace-cloud"
title="Preparing a new LAMP server on Rackspace Cloud"\>earlier
post\</a\>, try accessing /phpmyadmin on it now. It'll work. Not
good.\<br /\> \<h2\> Problem #2\</h2\> Not only are we exposing the URL
to phpMyAdmin with reckless abandon (check your server logs and I
guarantee you you'll find plenty of bots trying to access it after a
while), but we're exposing it over http, meaning all traffic is
unencrypted. The problem here should be fairly obvious - this is after
all your database which presumably will soon be full of lots of
important, potentially sensitive and valuable data - data you may be
obliged to keep private and almost certainly obliged to keep secure. We
need to get communication running over SSL, and we need to stop exposing
the default /phpmyadmin path.\<br /\> \<h2\> A solution\</h2\>
\<i\>A\</i\> solution - not necessarily \<i\>the\</i\> solution, is
fairly simple:\<br /\> \<ol\> \<li\>Get rid of the global
\<code\>Alias\</code\> directive\</li\> \<li\>Set up a new VirtualHost
to serve phpMyAdmin from\</li\> \<li\>Only expose this VirtualHost over
SSL\</li\> \</ol\> \<h2\> Setting up the VirtualHost\</h2\> Let's move
the phpmyadmin.conf file into /etc/apache2/sites-available and set about
getting rid of that Alias and wrapping the whole thing in a
VirtualHost:\<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\>nick@pd01:\~\$ sudo mv
/etc/apache2/conf.d/phpmyadmin.conf
/etc/apache2/sites-available/\</code\>\</pre\> Now edit the file with
your favourite editor (use sudo or you won't be able to write your
changes) and change it to look like the following:\<br /\>
\<pre\>\<code\>\<virtualhost\> ServerName my-fake-domain DocumentRoot
/usr/share/phpmyadmin \<directory phpmyadmin="" share="" usr=""\>
Options FollowSymLinks DirectoryIndex index.php \<ifmodule
mod_php5.c=""\> AddType application/x-httpd-php .php php_flag
magic_quotes_gpc Off php_flag track_vars On php_flag register_globals
Off php_value include_path . \</ifmodule\> \</directory\> \# Authorize
for setup \<directory phpmyadmin="" setup="" share="" usr=""\>
\<ifmodule mod_authn_file.c=""\> AuthType Basic AuthName"phpMyAdmin
Setup" AuthUserFile /etc/phpmyadmin/htpasswd.setup \</ifmodule\> Require
valid-user \</directory\> \# Disallow web access to directories that
don't need it \<directory libraries="" phpmyadmin="" share="" usr=""\>
Order Deny,Allow Deny from All \</directory\> \<directory lib=""
phpmyadmin="" setup="" share="" usr=""\> Order Deny,Allow Deny from All
\</directory\> \</virtualhost\> \</code\>\</pre\> All we've done here is
removed the Alias line, added two familiar VirtualHost specific
directives (ServerName and DocumentRoot), and wrapped the whole thing in
a VirtualHost declaration. I've chosen a ServerName which doesn't
actually resolve, so I'd have to add \<code\>my-fake-domain\</code\> to
the \<code\>/etc/hosts\</code\> file of each computer I wanted to access
phpMyAdmin from. You don't \<i\>need\</i\> this to be a real domain, so
you might as well choose a fake one to just reduce your attack surface
that little bit further.\<br /\> If you restart Apache now and try and
access the /phpmyadmin path you'll now get Apache's default 404 page but
won't be able to access your new VirtualHost (we haven't enabled it
yet) - so let's finish off our configuration.\<br /\> \<h2\> Setting up
SSL\</h2\> Assuming you've got \<b\>mod_ssl\</b\> enabled you should
have a VirtualHost template which we're going to pinch the relevant bits
from for this next step. Take a peak at
\<code\>/etc/apache2/sites-available/default-ssl\</code\> - it's quite
large so we won't duplicate it here, but it's worth having a quick read
over. We're only interested in a few lines:\<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\> \#
SSL Engine Switch: \# Enable/Disable SSL for this virtual host.
SSLEngine on

\# A self-signed (snakeoil) certificate can be created by installing \#
the ssl-cert package. See \#
/usr/share/doc/apache2.2-common/README.Debian.gz for more info. \# If
both key and certificate are stored in the same file, only the \#
SSLCertificateFile directive is needed. SSLCertificateFile
/etc/ssl/certs/ssl-cert-snakeoil.pem SSLCertificateKeyFile
/etc/ssl/private/ssl-cert-snakeoil.key\</code\>\</pre\> Let's add these
lines to our phpmyadmin.conf file - be sure to change the port the
VirtualHost is bound to from 80 to 443. We're also going to add a quick
RewriteRule to block requests with an incorrect http host header (more
on that later): \<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\> \<virtualhost\> ServerName
my-fake-domain DocumentRoot /usr/share/phpmyadmin

        RewriteEngine On
        RewriteCond %{HTTP_HOST} !my-fake-domain
        RewriteRule (.*) [L]

\<directory phpmyadmin="" share="" usr=""\> Options FollowSymLinks
DirectoryIndex index.php

\<ifmodule mod_php5.c=""\> AddType application/x-httpd-php .php

php_flag magic_quotes_gpc Off php_flag track_vars On php_flag
register_globals Off php_value include_path . \</ifmodule\>

\</directory\>

\# Authorize for setup \<directory phpmyadmin="" setup="" share=""
usr=""\> \<ifmodule mod_authn_file.c=""\> AuthType Basic
AuthName"phpMyAdmin Setup" AuthUserFile /etc/phpmyadmin/htpasswd.setup
\</ifmodule\> Require valid-user \</directory\>

\# Disallow web access to directories that don't need it \<directory
libraries="" phpmyadmin="" share="" usr=""\> Order Deny,Allow Deny from
All \</directory\> \<directory lib="" phpmyadmin="" setup="" share=""
usr=""\> Order Deny,Allow Deny from All \</directory\>

\# SSL Engine Switch: \# Enable/Disable SSL for this virtual host.
SSLEngine on

\# A self-signed (snakeoil) certificate can be created by installing \#
the ssl-cert package. See \#
/usr/share/doc/apache2.2-common/README.Debian.gz for more info. \# If
both key and certificate are stored in the same file, only the \#
SSLCertificateFile directive is needed. SSLCertificateFile
/etc/ssl/certs/ssl-cert-snakeoil.pem SSLCertificateKeyFile
/etc/ssl/private/ssl-cert-snakeoil.key \</virtualhost\>\</code\>\</pre\>
Now simply restart apache, navigate to
\<b\>https://my-fake-domain\</b\>, choose to ignore the security warning
(it only appears because the certificate is self-signed - the connection
is still secure), and voila - you'll be presented with the phpMyAdmin
login screen. You're done.\<br /\> \<h3\> A note on the
RewriteRule\</h3\> Apache's VirtualHost behaviour can be a little
confusing at first. It attempts to match the incoming http host header
to a known VirtualHost (e.g. looking for a corresponding ServerName or
ServerAlias somewhere in its loaded configuration files). If it can't
find a match, it serves the default - the first loaded - VirtualHost,
running on the appropriate port. This is important because we've only
got one VirtualHost running on SSL - and \<a
href="http://www.stombi.net/blog/post/2005/07/14/30-apache2-multiple-ssl-virtual-hosts"\>can
only have one\</a\>, so by simply visiting any domain on your server or
indeed its IP address over https, an attacker would be presented with
your phpmyadmin site. To counter this, we use a simple RewriteRule to
check if the http host header is correct - if not, we rewrite the
request to serve nothing. It's not the most elegant solution, but it
works well.\<br /\> \<h2\> Wrapping Up\</h2\> This post should serve as
a quick guide to avoiding some of the more common pitfalls encountered
when setting up phpMyAdmin, though of course it doesn't instantly solve
all your security concerns at once. You've still got to make sure your
database passwords are secure and you may find you out-grow the
phpmyadmin-as-a-vhost model quite quickly when you need more
applications running over SSL - but for a few minutes work it's well
worth doing and will thwart a lot of the simpler more speculative bots
looking for common server weaknesses.\</div\> \<br /\>
http://www.howtoforge.com/managing-multiple-mysql-servers-from-one-phpmyadmin-installation-using-ssl-encryption\<br
/\> http://askubuntu.com/questions/194074/enabling-ssl-in-mysql \<br /\>
\<br /\> \<table\>\<tbody\> \<tr\>\<td class="votecell"\>\<div
class="vote"\> \<span class="vote-count-post"\>3\</span\> \<a
class="vote-down-off" href="https://www.blogger.com/null" title="This
answer is not useful"\>down vote\</a\>

\</div\> \</td\>

\<td class="answercell"\>\<div class="post-text"\> Ubuntu 12.04 comes
with a OpenSSL 1.0.1, which has somewhat different defaults than the
older OpenSSL 0.9.8 version.\<br /\> Among other things, if you're using
\<code\>openssl req -newkey rsa:2048\</code\> to generate an RSA key,
you'll end up with a key in a format called \<a
href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PKCS_8" rel="nofollow"\>PKCS
#8\</a\>. Represented in the PEM format, these keys have the more
generic \<code\>-----BEGIN PRIVATE KEY-----\</code\> header, which
doesn't tell you what kind (RSA, DSA, EC) key it is.\<br /\> Previously,
with OpenSSL 0.9.8, keys were always in a format called \<a
href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PKCS_1" rel="nofollow"\>PKCS
#1\</a\>, which represented as PEM, had the header \<code\>-----BEGIN
RSA PRIVATE KEY-----\</code\>.\<br /\> Because of this you cannot simply
change the header and footer from:\<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\>-----BEGIN
PRIVATE KEY----- \</code\>\</pre\> to\<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\>-----BEGIN
RSA PRIVATE KEY-----\` \</code\>\</pre\> It's not the same thing and it
won't work. Instead you need to convert the key to the old format using
\<code\>openssl rsa\</code\>. Like this:\<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\>openssl
rsa -in key_in_pkcs1_or_pkcs8.pem -out key_in_pkcs1.pem
\</code\>\</pre\> MySQL (v5.5.35) on Ubuntu 12.04 is using an SSL
implementation called yaSSL (v2.2.2). It expect keys to be in the PKCS
#1 format and doesn't support the PKCS #8 format used by OpenSSL 1.0 and
newer. If you simply change the header and footer, as suggested by other
posts in this thread, MySQL/yaSSL won't complain, but you'll be unable
to connect and instead end up with an error like this:\<br /\>
\<pre\>\<code\>ERROR 2026 (HY000): SSL connection error: protocol
version mismatch \</code\>\</pre\> \<b\>Ubuntu 14.04\</b\> comes with
OpenSSL 1.0.1f and new settings. Among other things, it will generate
certificates with SHA256 digests instead of SHA1, which was used in
earlier versions.\
Incidentially, the yaSSL version bundled with MySQL doesn't support this
either.\<br /\> If you're generating certificates for use with MySQL,
remember to make sure the RSA keys are converted to the traditional PKCS
#1 PEM format and that certificates are using SHA1 digests.\<br /\>
Here's an example of how to generate your own CA, a server certificate
and a client certificate.\<br /\> \<pre\>\<code\># Generate a CA key and
certificate with SHA1 digest openssl genrsa 2048 &gt; ca-key.pem openssl
req -sha1 -new -x509 -nodes -days 3650 -key ca-key.pem &gt; ca-cert.pem

# Create server key and certficate with SHA1 digest, sign it and convert

# the RSA key from PKCS #8 (OpenSSL 1.0 and newer) to the old PKCS #1 format

openssl req -sha1 -newkey rsa:2048 -days 730 -nodes -keyout
server-key.pem &gt; server-req.pem openssl x509 -sha1 -req -in
server-req.pem -days 730 -CA ca-cert.pem -CAkey ca-key.pem -set_serial
01 &gt; server-cert.pem openssl rsa -in server-key.pem -out
server-key.pem

# Create client key and certificate with SHA digest, sign it and convert

# the RSA key from PKCS #8 (OpenSSL 1.0 and newer) to the old PKCS #1 format

openssl req -sha1 -newkey rsa:2048 -days 730 -nodes -keyout
client-key.pem &gt; client-req.pem openssl x509 -sha1 -req -in
client-req.pem -days 730 -CA ca-cert.pem -CAkey ca-key.pem -set_serial
01 &gt; client-cert.pem openssl rsa -in client-key.pem -out
client-key.pem \</code\>\</pre\> \</div\> \</td\>\</tr\>
\</tbody\>\</table\> \<br /\> \<br /\>

`<content type='html'>`{=html}\<h1\>
http://fideloper.com/ubuntu-12-04-lamp-server-setup \</h1\> \<h1\>
&nbsp;Ubuntu 12.04 LTS LAMP Server Setup\</h1\> \<ul class="tags meta
clearfix"\> \<li class="time"\>\<time\>1 year ago\</time\>\</li\> \<li
class="primary badge"\>\<a
href="http://fideloper.com/tag/ubuntu"\>ubuntu\</a\>\</li\> \<li
class="primary badge"\>\<a
href="http://fideloper.com/tag/server"\>server\</a\>\</li\> \<li
class="primary badge"\>\<a
href="http://fideloper.com/tag/cli"\>cli\</a\>\</li\> \</ul\> This will
go over getting an Ubuntu 12.04 LTS server up and running for production
use. Note: This does not pretend to be an exhaustive resource,
particularly around security. Additionally, if your environment is more
complex (Separate DB servers, servers across data-centers, different
access levels, etc), then your setup can and will vary.\<br /\> \<h4\>
Setup\</h4\> This will install some basic packages, including php
5.4.\<br /\> \<pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span
class="pln"\>\$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> update \$ sudo
apt\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>y vim \</span\>\<span
class="com"\># Everyone likes vim, right?\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>y build\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>essential \$ sudo
apt\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>y python\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>software\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>properties

\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Run these 2 steps if you want php 5.4,
rather than 5.3\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo add\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>apt\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>repository ppa\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>:\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>ondrej\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>php5 \$ sudo
apt\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> update

\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Install the LAMP
components\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>y php5 \$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>y apache2 \$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>y libapache2\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>mod\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>php5 \$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>y mysql\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>server \$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>y php5\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>mysql \$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>y php5\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>curl \$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>y php5\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>gd \$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>y php5\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>mcrypt

\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Set your server name (Avoid error message
on reload/restart of Apache)\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ echo
\</span\>\<span class="str"\>'ServerName localhost'\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>\|\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> sudo tee \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>httpd\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>conf

\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Enable mod-rewrite\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \$ sudo a2enmod rewrite\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> \<h4\>
Git\</h4\> You may need Git on your server depending on your deployment
strategy, or to support package managers such as Composer.\<br /\> \<pre
class="prettyprint prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="pln"\>\$ sudo
apt\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>y git\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>core\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> \<h4\> Composer\</h4\> If
you use Composer, you should also have it on your production server to
pull in dependencies. Note: For production use, you should lock in your
dependency version numbers. That way you won't get any surprises when
you update composer packages on your live server.\<br /\> \<pre
class="prettyprint prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="com"\># Install
composer globally\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ curl \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>sS https\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>:\</span\>\<span class="com"\>//getcomposer.org/installer
\| php\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo mv composer\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>phar \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>usr\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>local\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>bin\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>composer\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> \<h4\>
Tweaks/Security\</h4\> Here we'll make some light performance tweaks,
and adjust some settings for security.\<br /\> First, some providers
allow root login via SSH. We want to turn that off. I suggest opening a
new SSH connection immediately after creating a sudo user (in a separate
Terminal session/window) before doing this, just in case you lock
yourself out by accident.\<br /\> If your provider gives you a login
other than "root", then you likely have a sudo user already and can skip
the step of creating a sudo user. However, you should still ensure that
you cannot log in as root.\<br /\> \<pre class="prettyprint
prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="com"\># Create a new sudo
user\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ adduser mysudouser \</span\>\<span
class="com"\># Create user\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ usermod
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>G sudo
mysudouser \</span\>\<span class="com"\># Make user a sudo user
(sudoer)\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>

\</span\>\<span class="com"\># (Log in and make sure this sudo user does
indeed have the sudo permissiosn)\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>

\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Don't let root login in via
ssh\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo vim \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>ssh\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>sshd_config \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="typ"\>PermitRootLogin\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>no\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Change from yes\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \$ sudo reload ssh\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> I typically
also create a user for deployment. This user will share the same primary
group as apache (www-data), and so will be able to read/write the
web-server files. This is not a sudo user.\<br /\> \<pre
class="prettyprint prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="com"\># Deploy
user\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ adduser mydeployuser \$ usermod
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>g
www\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>data
mydeployuser\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> Here are some performance tweaks
for Apache. We'll decrease the timeout time, and allow more keep-alive
requests.\<br /\> \<pre class="prettyprint
prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="com"\># Apache
tweaks\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo vim \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>conf \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="typ"\>Timeout\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="lit"\>45\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="com"\># Change from 300\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="typ"\>MaxKeepAliveRequests\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="lit"\>200\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="com"\># Change from
100\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> Here are security tweaks. We'll turn off
how much information about the server is returned in the HTTP
headers.\<br /\> \<pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span
class="pln"\>\$ sudo nano \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>conf\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>d\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>security \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="typ"\>ServerTokens\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="typ"\>Prod\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="com"\># Change from 'OS' or any
other\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="typ"\>ServerSignature\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="typ"\>Off\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Change from
'On'\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> These are general PHP settings to tweak.
Bump up the file size for file uploads, but decrease how many can be
uploaded at once. \<b\>As a security tweak, also turn off the display of
which PHP version is being used\</b\>.\<br /\> \<pre class="prettyprint
prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="pln"\>\$ sudo nano \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>php5\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>php\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>ini \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> post_max_size
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>=\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="lit"\>8M\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Change to 8M\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
upload_max_filesize \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>=\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="lit"\>8M\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="com"\># Change from
2M\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> max_file_uploads
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>=\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="lit"\>5\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Change from 20\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> expose_php \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>=\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> off \</span\>\<span class="com"\># Change fron
'On'\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo service apache2
restart\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> The directory
\<code\>/var/www\</code\> is the main web-root. The following will give
everything in the web root the Apache user and group. This way Apache
and the 'deploy' user are the only ones who can read/write web files.
\<b\>Note:\</b\> This makes use of \<a
href="http://fideloper.com/user-group-permissions-chmod-apache"
title="apache group permissions"\>group permissions\</a\>. The following
is saying "Users and Groups can read and write these files, but other
users can only read them".\<br /\> \<pre class="prettyprint
prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="com"\># Web-root
permissions\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo chown \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>R www\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>data\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>:\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>www\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>data \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>var\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>www \</span\>\<span
class="com"\># make sure same owner:group\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\$ sudo chmod \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>R go\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>rwx \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>var\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>www \</span\>\<span class="com"\># Remove all group/other
permissions\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo chmod \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>R g\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>+\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>rw \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>var\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>www \</span\>\<span
class="com"\># Add group read/write\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo
chmod \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>R
o\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>+\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>r
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>var\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>www \</span\>\<span class="com"\># Allow other to read
only\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> \<h3\> Virtual Hosts\</h3\> This is a
command-line tool I created for \<a
href="https://gist.github.com/fideloper/2710970"\>generating a virtual
host\</a\> within Apache (Ubuntu specific). This will enable the use of
.htaccess files and turn off index listings by default. It also sets up
log files per virtual host.\<br /\> \<pre class="prettyprint
prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="com"\># vhosts\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \$ curl https\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>:\</span\>\<span
class="com"\>//gist.github.com/fideloper/2710970/raw/6b5fd9de45f75e613178d296e87f586ca5b61220/vhost.sh
&gt; /usr/local/bin/vhost\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ chmod
guo\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>+\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>x
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>usr\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>local\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>bin\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>vhost \$ sudo vhost \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>h \</span\>\<span
class="com"\># See the available options\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\>
\<h4\> Firewall\</h4\> This is exactly as per \<a
href="https://www.digitalocean.com/community/articles/how-to-set-up-a-firewall-using-ip-tables-on-ubuntu-12-04"\>here\</a\>.
It will allow port 22 (or current ssh port), 80 and 443 (ssh, web
traffic, ssl web traffic respectively). It also gives loopback access,
important if your server is virtualized (chances are, it is).\<br /\>
\<pre class="prettyprint prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="com"\>#
Run as root or use sudo\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo iptables
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>A INPUT
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>m conntrack
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>--\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>ctstate
ESTABLISHED\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>,\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>RELATED \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>j ACCEPT \$ sudo iptables \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>A INPUT \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>p tcp \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>--\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>dport ssh \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>j ACCEPT \$ sudo iptables
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>A INPUT
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>p tcp
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>--\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>dport
\</span\>\<span class="lit"\>80\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>j ACCEPT \$
sudo iptables \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>A INPUT \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>p tcp \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>--\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>dport \</span\>\<span class="lit"\>443\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>j ACCEPT \$ sudo iptables \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>A INPUT \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>j DROP \$ sudo iptables
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>I INPUT
\</span\>\<span class="lit"\>1\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>i lo
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>j ACCEPT

\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Install so firewalls are saved through
restarts\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo apt\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> install \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>y iptables\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>persistent \$ sudo service iptables\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>persistent
start\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> \<h4\> Add MySQL user\</h4\> This will
create a MySQL user for your application to use. Note the example below
will grant \<b\>all\</b\> permissions. You should be as restrictive as
possible, giving only what's necessary. In many instances, MySQL users
will will be OK with simply having SELECT, UPDATE, DELETE, and INSERT
privileges, but there are \<a
href="http://dev.mysql.com/doc/refman/5.1/en/privileges-provided.html"\>many
more privileges\</a\> to choose from. Additionally, any user who will be
used to \<code\>mysqldump\</code\> will need the LOCK TABLES
privilege.\<br /\> Also note that if you have a MySQL database on a
separate server, you'll need to change \<code\>localhost\</code\> to the
IP or host name of the server connecting to the database. There is also
some more work to allow remote connections on MySQL (Editing my.cnf
\<code\>bind-address\</code\> and using firewalls to only allow MySQL
connections on the same local network is one strategy).\<br /\> \<pre
class="prettyprint prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="pln"\>\$ mysql
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>u root
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>p
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> CREATE
USER \</span\>\<span class="str"\>'user'\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>@\</span\>\<span class="str"\>'localhost'\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> IDENTIFIED BY \</span\>\<span
class="str"\>'password'\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>;\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> GRANT ALL PRIVILEGES ON database\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>.\*\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> TO \</span\>\<span
class="str"\>'user'\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>@\</span\>\<span
class="str"\>'localhost'\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>;\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> \<h4\> Add SSL\</h4\> If you
need to install an SSL certificate, this has worked for me when
installing a (non-premium) SSL. This assumes a 1-year SSL, with 2048
encryption. YMMV.\<br /\> \<pre class="prettyprint
prettyprinted"\>\<code\>\<span class="pln"\>\$ sudo a2enmod ssl
\</span\>\<span class="com"\># Enable loading of SSL
module\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo service apache2 restart \$
sudo mkdir \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>ssl \$ cd \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>ssl \</span\>\<span class="com"\># Change the domain from
"yourdomain.com" to what you need\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \$ sudo
openssl req \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>new\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>days \</span\>\<span
class="lit"\>365\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>nodes \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>newkey rsa\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>:\</span\>\<span class="lit"\>2048\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>keyout yourdomain\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>com\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>key \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span class="kwd"\>out\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> yourdomain\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>com\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>csr \$ sudo chmod \</span\>\<span
class="lit"\>400\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> yourdomain\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>com\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>key \</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>...\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> add csr\</span\>\<span
class="pun"\>,\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="kwd"\>get\</span\>\<span class="pln"\> key back \$ sudo vim
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>sites\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>-\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>available\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>your_vhost\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>conf \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span class="typ"\>SSLEngine\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> on \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="typ"\>SSLCertificateFile\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>ssl\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>yourdomain\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>com\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>crt \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="typ"\>SSLCertificateKeyFile\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>ssl\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>yourdomain\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>com\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>key \</span\>\<span class="pun"\>&gt;\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\> \</span\>\<span
class="typ"\>SSLCertificateChainFile\</span\>\<span class="pln"\>
\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>etc\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>apache2\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>ssl\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>/\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>sf_bundle\</span\>\<span class="pun"\>.\</span\>\<span
class="pln"\>crt\</span\>\</code\>\</pre\> And that's it - These steps
will get you started on having a usable Ubuntu 12.04 server.\<br /\>
\<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\> &nbsp;MYSQL\<br /\>

`</content>`{=html}`<link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://lonurhazve.blogspot.com/2014/04/httpfideloper.html#comment-form' title='0 Comments'/>`{=html}`<link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/2421391777999081184'/>`{=html}`<link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/2421391777999081184'/>`{=html}`<author>`{=html}`<name>`{=html}lonurhazve`</name>`{=html}`<uri>`{=html}https://www.blogger.com/profile/16306879527733710247`</uri>`{=html}`<email>`{=html}noreply@blogger.com`</email>`{=html}`<gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='35' height='35' src='//www.blogger.com/img/blogger_logo_round_35.png'/>`{=html}`</author>`{=html}`<thr:total>`{=html}0`</thr:total>`{=html}`</entry>`{=html}`<entry>`{=html}`<id>`{=html}tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-702950587710156521.post-7746837997625742265`</id>`{=html}`<published>`{=html}2014-04-27T22:14:00.001+08:00`</published>`{=html}`<updated>`{=html}2014-04-27T22:14:59.810+08:00`</updated>`{=html}`<app:control xmlns:app='http://purl.org/atom/app#'>`{=html}`<app:draft>`{=html}yes`</app:draft>`{=html}`</app:control>`{=html}`<category scheme='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#kind' term='http://schemas.google.com/blogger/2008/kind#post'/>`{=html}
