`<content type='html'>`{=html}\<h2\>
http://www.pc-freak.net/blog/disable-debian-gnu-linux-squeeze-apache-2-version-reporting-improve-security/
\</h2\> \<h2\> How to disable Debian GNU / Linux (Squeeze) Apache 2
version reporting to improve security\</h2\> \<div class="adsense"
style="float: right; margin: 12px;"\> \</div\> Debian GNU / Linux's
Apache default behavior is to \<i\>report Apache server name, version
and Linux distribution version and codename\</i\>.\<br /\> This is shown
as a minor security leak in many Security Scanner (audit) software like
Nessus. It reveals a vital information which could help malicious
attacker later to use exploit if the version number in question is
vulnerable.\<br /\> The quickest way to check, either Apache versioning
and distro info is disabled is with \<i\>telnet\</i\>:\<br /\>
\<blockquote\> hipo@noah:\~/Desktop\$ telnet pc-freak.net 80\<br /\>
Trying 83.228.93.76...\<br /\> Connected to pc-freak.net.\<br /\> Escape
character is '\^\]'.\<br /\> HEAD / HTTP/1.0\<br /\> Connection closed
by foreign host.\<br /\> hipo@noah:\~/Desktop\$ telnet pc-freak.net
80\<br /\> Trying 83.228.93.76...\<br /\> Connected to pc-freak.net.\<br
/\> Escape character is '\^\]'.\<br /\> HEAD / HTTP/1.0\<br /\> HTTP/1.1
200 OK\<br /\> Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2012 10:48:36 GMT\<br /\> Server:
Apache/2.2.16 (Debian)\<br /\> X-Powered-By: PHP/5.3.3-7+squeeze14\<br
/\> Vary: Accept-Encoding\<br /\> Connection: close\<br /\>
Content-Type: text/html \</blockquote\> Disabling this \<i\>Distro
version codename and version number reporting\</i\> on Debian is done by
changing in file \<b\>/etc/apache2/conf.d/security\</b\> directives:\<br
/\> \<code\>\<br /\> ServerTokens OS\<br /\> ServerSignature On\<br /\>
\</code\>\<br /\> to\<br /\> \<code\>\<br /\> ServerSignature Off\<br
/\> ServerTokens ProductOnly\<br /\> \</code\>\<br /\> Here important
note to make is if you try adding:\<br /\> \<b\>ServerSignature
Off\</b\> and \<b\>ServerTokens Prod\</b\> straight in Debian general
config \<i\>/etc/apache2/apache2.conf\</i\>, but did not change the
settings set for the vars through
\<i\>/etc/apache2/conf.d/security\</i\>; settings from
\<i\>/etc/apache2/conf.d/security\</i\> will overwrite
\<i\>ServerSignature / ServerTokens\</i\> settings set in
\<b\>/etc/apache2/apache2.conf\</b\>\<br /\> I tried this myself
(forgotting about /etc/apache2/conf.d/security) and adding both
variables straight in \<i\>apache2.conf\</i\>. After Apache restart
Apache version number and type of distribution continued be returned by
the WebServer.\<br /\> I thought something specific changed in
\<i\>Debian Squeeze -- Apache/2.2.16\</i\> so this two variables are
probably not working so I did a quick research online seing other people
complaining also \<i\>unable to disable Apache ver and Linux distro
version\</i\> and looking for a reason why. Well anyways if you happen
to also ponder, why \<i\>ServerSignature Off\</i\> and \<i\>ServerTokens
ProductOnly\</i\> does not take effect keep in mind it is due to
overwritten settings via \<i\>/etc/apache2/conf.d/security\</i\>,
changing the values there and restarting Apache and you're done \<img
alt=":)" class="wp-smiley"
src="http://www.pc-freak.net/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif"
/\> \<br /\> To make sure 100% Apache is no longer returning exact
version number and host installed distro type, use \<i\>telnet\</i\>
again:\<br /\> \<blockquote\> hipo@noah:\~/Desktop\$ telnet pc-freak.net
80\<br /\> Trying 83.228.93.76...\<br /\> Connected to pc-freak.net.\<br
/\> Escape character is '\^\]'.\<br /\> HEAD / HTTP/1.0\<br /\>
Connection closed by foreign host. \</blockquote\> \<br /\>
http://howto.biapy.com/en/debian-gnu-linux/servers/apache-2/harden-the-security-of-apache-2-on-debian
\<br /\> \<br /\> \<h1 class="documentFirstHeading"\>

        &lt;span class="" id="parent-fieldname-title-8a83d0f32d654391a27d93cb5125ad84"&gt;
            Harden the security of Apache 2 on Debian
        &lt;/span&gt;

        &lt;/h1&gt;

\<div class="documentByLine" id="plone-document-byline"\> \<span
class="documentAuthor"\>

      by
      &lt;a href="http://howto.biapy.com/en/author/pierre-yves"&gt;Pierre-Yves Landuré&lt;/a&gt;
      
         —
    &lt;/span&gt;

\<span class="documentModified"\>

      last modified

    Apr 23, 2014 11:47 

\</span\>

\</div\> \<div class="row" id="portlets-below"\> \</div\> \<div
class="RatingViewlet"\> \</div\> \<div class="documentDescription"\>
\<span class=""
id="parent-fieldname-description-8a83d0f32d654391a27d93cb5125ad84"\>
Apache 2 is a robust HTTP server with numerous functionalities. This
howto harden the security of Apache 2 by apply basic rules. \</span\>

        &lt;/div&gt;

This howto is tested on:\<br /\> \<ul\> \<li\>Debian 6.0 Squeeze\</li\>
\<li\>Debian 7.0 Wheezy\</li\> \</ul\> \<h2\> Prerequisites\</h2\> This
howto needs :\<br /\> \<ul\> \<li\>A Apache 2 HTTP as described by \<a
class="internal-link"
href="http://howto.biapy.com/en/debian-gnu-linux/servers/apache-2/install-and-setup-apache-2-on-debian"\>Install
and setup Apache 2 on Debian\</a\>.\</li\> \</ul\> \<span
id="result_box"\>\<span class="hps"\>This howto recommends\</span\>
:\</span\>\<br /\> \<ul\> \<li\>\<span id="result_box"\> \<span
class="hps"\>the\</span\>\<span class="hps"\>\</span\> DFind \<span
class="hps"\>blocking rules\</span\> \<span class="hps"\>described
by\</span\> \</span\>\<a class="internal-link"
href="http://howto.biapy.com/en/debian-gnu-linux/system/security/block-the-vulnerability-scanner-dfind"
target="\_self" title=""\>\<span class="internal-link"\>Block the
vulnerability scanner \</span\>\<span
class="internal-link"\>DFind\</span\>\</a\>.\</li\> \</ul\> \<h2\>
Configuration\</h2\> \<h3\> Harden Apache 2 HTTP server
configuration\</h3\> Apply some rules hardening server security:\<br /\>
\<pre\>command wget
'https://raw.github.com/biapy/howto.biapy.com/master/apache2/security-hardened.conf'\
--quiet --no-check-certificate
--output-document='/etc/apache2/conf.d/security-hardened'\</pre\> Reload
server configuration:\<br /\> \<pre\>/etc/init.d/apache2 reload\</pre\>
\<h3\> Block attacks with fail2ban\</h3\> Install fail2ban :\<br /\>
\<pre\>command apt-get install fail2ban\</pre\> Enable the Apache 2
protection rules:\<br /\> \<pre\>if \[ ! -e '/etc/fail2ban/jail.local'
\]; then command touch '/etc/fail2ban/jail.local' fi if \[ -z
"\$(command grep"\[apache\]" '/etc/fail2ban/jail.local')" \]; then echo
"\[apache\] enabled = true

\[apache-noscript\] enabled = true

\[apache-overflows\] enabled = true " &gt;&gt;
'/etc/fail2ban/jail.local' fi\</pre\> Reload the configuration :\<br /\>
\<pre\>/etc/init.d/fail2ban restart\</pre\> \<h3\> Disable the cgi-bin
folder\</h3\> The cgi-bin folder use has been deprecated by script
languages such as PHP. Its presence can be a security issue. Disable
it:\<br /\> \<pre\>command sed -i\
-e 's\|\^.*ScriptAlias.*/cgi-bin/.\*$|#\0|' \
 -e '/Directory.*cgi-bin/,/\/Directory/s/^.*/#\0/' \
 "/etc/apache2/sites-available/default"{,-ssl}&lt;/pre&gt; Reload the configuration :&lt;br /&gt; &lt;pre&gt;/etc/init.d/apache2 force-reload&lt;/pre&gt; &lt;pre&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/pre&gt; &lt;br /&gt; http://nerdartnerd.blogspot.com/2014/01/howto-securing-apache-webserver-with.html &lt;br /&gt; &lt;h3 class="post-title entry-title"&gt; &lt;a href="http://nerdartnerd.blogspot.com/2014/01/howto-securing-apache-webserver-with.html"&gt;HowTo: Securing apache webserver with mod-security on Debian wheezy&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class="post-header"&gt; &lt;/div&gt; The most common attack vector against publicly exposed servers is exploiting vulnerabilities in the services those servers provide. Webservers are a welcome target for crackers and script-kiddies: misconfigured servers or buggy software make an easy prey for hacking into.&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; The following is a very wide-spread, very simple and often successful attack that can be prevented by using mod-security:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; The attacker finds a vulnerable script that has write access to the server's file system. This can be done by&lt;br /&gt; - using security-scanner software,&lt;br /&gt; - blind or educated guess or&lt;br /&gt; - by using a known vulnerability in a publicly available service&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; Then the attacker uses this script to alter a file or upload malware to the server:&lt;br /&gt; this may be a sneaky change to an already existing script which opens a backdoor or some kind of webshell or ircbot.&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; If that already happened to you: Congratulations, you're now the proud owner of a freshly infected zombie!&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; If you are a sysadmin and running one ore more webservers with apache you may have been wondering how you could protect those machines from being compromised. There are a few steps you should take before you follow this quick introduction to mod-security:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;1.&lt;/b&gt; Make sure apache is configured properly. Try to restrict the server from sending unnecessary information about its version, installed  services etc. Search and read articles about hardening webservices and apache. Understand how attackers gather information about your servers and what kind of vulnerablity they could be after.&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;2.&lt;/b&gt; Do not run exploitable software. Common targets are unpatched versions of Wordpress etc., webmail-services, and CMSs. If possible, try  to restrict access to or avoid tools like phpmyadmin. &lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;3. &lt;/b&gt;Make sure potentially exploitable scripts, like php, have no way to write on the filesystem. This is not always practical, but should  be manageable: use a development system for file uploads and merge changes into your (read-only) public production system. You may want to use wget to take an html-only-snapshot of your development system for deployment on your production system.&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;4.&lt;/b&gt; If your web-folder (like /var/www) contains any files or directories with permissions like 0777, you're likely to experience problems in the near future. Be sure to understand what you are doing and try to explain your concerns to your users/web-developers. Database access should be configured read-only where no writing to the database is needed.&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; But now let's start with the HowTo:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;a href="http://www.modsecurity.org/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;mod-security&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is a very good tool for professionally securing webservers. Once you spent some time with it you wouldn't want to run a webserver without it. By design,  mod-security is a web application firewall (WAF) that blocks potentially dangerous requests to your server. But even without taking any action, just by logging, mod-sec can show you how bots or attackers try to exploit your services.&lt;br /&gt; I wrote this HowTo because I could not find any recent documentation on how to quickly set up mod-security on Debian wheezy. This really is only  a quick and superficial way to get mod-sec working. Be sure to read further documentation on how to set up and maintain this magnificent tool. (And please point out to me any mistakes I made or possible improvements to this HowTo).&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; This documentation &lt;b&gt;has only been tested on Debian wheezy&lt;/b&gt; (7.3 as of now). It is likely to be broken on any other distro or version.&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; I'm assuming apache is configured and running. Start by installing mod-security. Note that apache will be restarted in the process:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;# apt-get install libapache2-modsecurity&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; The module is now up and running. It is in no way configured yet, so it still does nothing. Let's configure mod-sec: if your installation went right you now have a set of rules under /usr/share/modsecurity-crs&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; If you're using wheezy, the config-files are under /etc/modsecurity&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; Copy the default rules:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;# cp -rp&amp;nbsp; /usr/share/modsecurity-crs/* /etc/modsecurity&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; Make an initial configuration:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;# cd /etc/modsecurity&lt;br /&gt;# cp -p modsecurity.conf-recommended modsecurity.conf&lt;br /&gt;# vi modsecurity.conf&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;Important:&lt;/b&gt; the first directive controls mod-sec's behaviour. Until everything is configured and your rules are O.K. it should look like this:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;SecRuleEngine DetectionOnly&amp;nbsp;&lt;/b&gt; # Do not block anything, just write logs&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; If you're satisfied, here is nothing more to do right now. Enable the configuration in apache:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;# vi /etc/apache2/conf.d/mod-security&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; with the following content:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;&lt;ifmodule security2_module=""&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp; Include /etc/modsecurity/*.conf&lt;br /&gt;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp; Include /etc/modsecurity/activated_rules/*.conf&lt;/ifmodule&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; Activate all rules in /etc/modsecurity/activated_rules by setting symlinks:&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;# cd /etc/modsecurity&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; &lt;b&gt;# for f in `ls base_rules/` ; do ln -s /etc/modsecurity/base_rules/$f
activated_rules/$f ; done&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt; &lt;br /&gt; ### As the name says the following is optional.&lt;br /&gt; ### Some of those rules may lead to PCRE-recursion-limit&lt;br /&gt; ### exceptions or missing data errors,&lt;br /&gt; ### depending on your configuration.&lt;br /&gt; # for f in `ls optional_rules/` ; do ln -s /etc/modsecurity/optional_rules/$f
activated_rules/\$f ; done\<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\> The preparations
are done now. Test the configuration:\<br /\> \<br /\> \<b\># apachectl
configtest\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> You should be getting "Syntax OK" - If
not, you're up to some trouble-shooting; please consult your
search-engine of choice for solutions - there are plenty!\<br /\> \<br
/\> If you got a "Syntax OK" you're fine. Time to restart apache:\<br
/\> \<br /\> \<b\># service apache2 restart\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> if
the server is very busy there should be plenty of false-positives now in
/var/log/apache2/modsec_audit.log\<br /\> That's O.K. for now: mod-sec
is up and running.\<br /\> If there is not enough traffic to trigger
alarms you may want to use a security-scanner such as nessus etc. or
some simple SQL-injection-attempt to trigger positive alarms.\<br /\>
\<br /\> Now you need to understand the logged errors and find false
positives. The better way to cope with those errors is to modify the
rule that triggered the alarm to your needs. The fast and insecure way
is to deactivate the rule by whitelisting. You can create a
whitelist-file with the following example content to whitelist
rules:\<br /\> \<br /\> \<b\># vi
/etc/modsecurity/activated_rules/modsecurity_crs_99_whitelist.conf\</b\>\<br
/\> \<br /\> content:\<br /\> \<b\># This client is allowed to bypass
mod-sec:\</b\>\<br /\> \<b\>#SecRule REMOTE_ADDR "\^192.168.0.3"
phase:1,nolog,allow,ctl:ruleEngine=off \<br /\>#SecRuleRemoveById 90001
\# deactivated rule\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\> To activate the
changes you need to reload your apache-configuration (I prefer a
restart).\<br /\> \<br /\> When you're confident that the rules are set
up correctly you can activate mod-sec's blocking engine in
/etc/modsec/modsecurity.conf:\<br /\> \<br /\> \<b\>SecRuleEngine
On\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\> That's it!\<br /\> To even further
secure your server you could use a tool like fail2ban to block IPs after
a certain amount of alarms or logcheck to send you email-notifications
on security events.\<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\>
&nbsp;http://secure-ubuntu-server.blogspot.com/2011/05/howto-secure-your-ubuntu-server-in.html\<br
/\> \<h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name"\> HOWTO : Secure
your Ubuntu Server in a passive way on Ubuntu 11.04 \</h3\> \<div
class="post-header"\> \</div\> \<b\>Root account access
warning\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> Add the following to the top of the file
\<code\>/root/.bashrc\</code\> and you will be informed by email when
the root account is being accessed.\<br /\> \<br /\> \<code\>echo -e
"Root Shell Access on `tty` `\n `{=tex}`w`" \| mail -s "Alert: Root
Access" samiux@gmail.com\</code\>\<br /\> \<br /\> You are also required
to add the captioned line at the sudoers' .bashrc file.\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<code\>echo -e "Sudoer Shell Access on `tty` `\n `{=tex}`w`" \| mail -s
"Alert: Sudoer Access" samiux@gmail.com\</code\>\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<b\>Hardening SSH\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\> The official port of SSH is
22. You can change it to any port that between 1024 and 65535. You can
do it at the router or firewall and you can do it at the configure file
of SSH at \<code\>/etc/ssh/sshd_config\</code\>. You are recommended to
disable the root account login via SSH even you are using Ubuntu.\<br
/\> \<br /\> \<code\>Port 65535\<br /\>PermitRootLogin no\</code\>\<br
/\> \<br /\> \<code\>sudo /etc/init.d/sshd restart\</code\>\<br /\> \<br
/\> \<br /\>
\<code\>&nbsp;http://www.cyberciti.biz/faq/apt-get-apticron-send-email-upgrades-available/\</code\>\<br
/\> \<div class="headline_area"\> \<h1 class="entry-title"\> Debian /
Ubuntu Linux: Send Automatic Email Notification When Security Upgrades
Available\</h1\> \<div class="headline_meta"\> by \<span class="author
vcard"\>\<a class="url fn" href="http://www.cyberciti.biz/tips/about-us"
rel="author"\>Nix Craft\</a\>\</span\> on \<abbr class="published"
title="2008-06-18"\>June 18, 2008\</abbr\> · \<a
href="http://www.cyberciti.biz/faq/apt-get-apticron-send-email-upgrades-available/#comments"
rel="nofollow"\>11 comments\</a\>· LAST UPDATED \<abbr class="updated"
title="2008-07-06"\>July 6, 2008\</abbr\>\</div\> \<div
class="headline_meta"\> in \<a
href="http://www.cyberciti.biz/faq/category/bash-shell/" rel="tag"\>BASH
Shell\</a\>, \<a
href="http://www.cyberciti.biz/faq/category/debian-ubuntu/"
rel="tag"\>Debian / Ubuntu\</a\>, \<a
href="http://www.cyberciti.biz/faq/category/email-servers/"
rel="tag"\>EMail Servers\</a\>\</div\> \</div\> \<div style="float:
right; margin-left: 5px; margin-top: 0px;"\> \<a
href="http://www.cyberciti.biz/faq/category/debian-ubuntu/" title="See
all Debian/Ubuntu Linux related FAQ"\>\<img border="0"
src="http://figs.cyberciti.biz/3rdparty/debianlogo.gif"
/\>\</a\>\</div\> \<span style="color: red;"\>Q.\</span\> How do I force
apt-get to send me email when upgrades or security updates available
under Debian or Ubuntu Linux? Do I need to write a shell script which
generates a mail with a list of all packages currently pending an
upgrade?\<br /\> \<span id="more-1131"\>\</span\>\<br /\> \<span
style="color: #009900;"\>A.\</span\> No you don't have to write a shell
script. You need to use apticron command / script for notification.
apticron is mainly intended for automatic notification of pending
security updates but can also be used in many other situations where
timely updates are neccessary.\<br /\> \<h2\> Install apticron\</h2\>
Type the following command at a shell prompt:\<br /\> \<code\># apt-get
update\<br /\> \# apt-get install apticron\</code\>\<br /\> \<h3\>
Configure apticron to send email notifications\</h3\> The default
coniguration file is located at /etc/apticron/apticron.conf. Open file
using text editor:\<br /\> \<code\># vi
/etc/apticron/apticron.conf\</code\>\<br /\> You need to set email
address to email the notification as follows:\<br /\>
\<code\>EMAIL="vivek@nixcraft.in"\</code\>\<br /\> \<br /\> \<h2\>
1.\<b\>&nbsp;Firewall \</b\>- UFW\</h2\> \<ul\> \<li\> A good place to
start is to install a Firewall.&nbsp;\</li\> \<li\> UFW - Uncomplicated
Firewall is a basic firewall that works very well and easy to configure
with its Firewall configuration tool -&nbsp;gufw,&nbsp;or
use&nbsp;&nbsp;Shorewall, fwbuilder, or Firestarter.\</li\> \<li\> Use
Firestarter&nbsp;GUI to configure your firewall or refer to the \<a
href="https://help.ubuntu.com/12.04/serverguide/firewall.html"
target="\_blank"\>Ubuntu Server Guide\</a\>, &nbsp;\<a
href="http://manpages.ubuntu.com/manpages/precise/en/man8/ufw.8.html"
target="\_blank"\>UFW manual pages\</a\> or the \<a
href="http://help.ubuntu.com/community/UFW" target="\_blank"\>Ubuntu
UFW&nbsp;community documentation\</a\>.\</li\> \<li\> Install UFW and
enable, open a terminal window and enter :\</li\> \</ul\> \<pre\>\<span
style="font-size: 14px;"\>sudo apt-get install ufw \</span\>\</pre\>
\<ul\> \<li\> Allow SSH and Http services.\</li\> \</ul\> \<pre\>\<span
style="font-size: 14px;"\>sudo ufw allow ssh sudo ufw allow http
\</span\>\</pre\> \<ul\> \<li\> Enable the firewall.\</li\> \</ul\>
\<pre\>\<span style="font-size: 14px;"\>sudo ufw enable
\</span\>\</pre\> \<ul\> \<li\> Check the status of the firewall.\</li\>
\</ul\> \<pre\>\<span style="font-size: 14px;"\>sudo ufw status
verbose&nbsp;\</span\>\</pre\> \<pre\>\<span style="font-size:
14px;"\>&nbsp;\</span\>\</pre\> \<pre\>\<span style="font-size:
14px;"\>&nbsp;\</span\>\</pre\> \<h2\> Admin user setup\</h2\> \<h3\>
Create the admin user\</h3\> \<code class="haskell" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>apt\</span\>-get install sudo \<span
class="title"\>adduser\</span\> adminuser \<span
class="title"\>usermod\</span\> -a -\<span class="label"\>G\</span\>
sudo adminuser \<span class="title"\>groupadd\</span\> admin \<span
class="title"\>usermod\</span\> -a -\<span class="label"\>G\</span\>
admin adminuser \<span class="title"\>dpkg\</span\>-statoverride \<span
class="comment"\>--update --add root admin 4750 /bin/su\</span\>
\</code\>

This creates our \<code style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>adminuser\</code\>
and adds him to the \<code style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo\</code\>
and \<code style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>admin\</code\> group which is
the now the only other group that can su with root.\<br /\> Ok let's
harden, or even soften for now our sudoers file, but before that change
the default editor. List the available editors first to make sure vim is
there:\<br /\> \<code class="sql" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span
class="operator"\>\<span class="keyword"\>update\</span\>-alternatives
--list editor sudo \<span class="keyword"\>update\</span\>-alternatives
--\<span class="keyword"\>set\</span\> editor /usr/bin/vim.basic visudo
\</span\>\</code\>

Add this to limit the time the sudo password is remembered:\<br /\>
\<code class="undefined" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>Defaults
timestamp_timeout=10 \</code\>

We will also make it so that our admin user will not have to enter his
password on sudo, at least during setup, you can change it back after.
Make sure you add this at the END of the file, so it is not over written
by the %sudo line. Once our major setting up is done\<br /\> \<code
class="vhdl" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>adminuser \<span
class="keyword"\>ALL\</span\>=(\<span class="keyword"\>ALL\</span\>)
NOPASSWD: \<span class="keyword"\>ALL\</span\> \</code\>

You can also add this instead of adding the user to the \<code
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo\</code\> group:\<br /\> \<code
class="vhdl" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\[your username\] \<span
class="keyword"\>ALL\</span\>=(\<span
class="keyword"\>ALL\</span\>:\<span class="keyword"\>ALL\</span\>)
\<span class="keyword"\>ALL\</span\> \</code\>

But I find it cleaner to manage what you can do via groups, which we
will do again later.\<br /\> We can now sudo with our new user, let's
log back on:\<br /\> \<code class="haskell" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>exit\</span\> \<span
class="title"\>ssh\</span\> adminuser@linodedomain.com \</code\>

\<a href="https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg#top"\>^top^\</a\>\<br /\> \<br
/\> \<br /\> \<pre\>\<span style="font-size:
14px;"\>&nbsp;\</span\>\</pre\> \<pre\>\<span style="font-size:
14px;"\>&nbsp;https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg\</span\>\</pre\> \<h2\>
Harden network\</h2\> \<h3\> sysctl\</h3\> \<code class="avrasm"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo \<span class="keyword"\>cp\</span\>
/etc/sysctl\<span class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\> /etc/sysctl\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.back\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\> sudo vim /etc/sysctl\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\> \</code\>

Last reminder to backup your config files default ;)\<br /\> \<code
class="avrasm"\> \<span class="preprocessor"\># Make server reboot on
low memory\</span\> vm\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.panic\</span\>\_on_oom=\<span
class="number"\>1\</span\> kernel\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.panic\</span\>=\<span class="number"\>10\</span\>

\<span class="preprocessor"\># Specific to Linode, experiment.\</span\>
vm\<span class="preprocessor"\>.swappiness\</span\>=\<span
class="number"\>25\</span\>

\<span class="preprocessor"\># IP Spoofing protection\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.all\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.rp\</span\>\_filter = \<span
class="number"\>1\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.default\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.rp\</span\>\_filter = \<span
class="number"\>1\</span\>

\<span class="preprocessor"\># Ignore ICMP broadcast requests\</span\>
net\<span class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.icmp\</span\>\_echo_ignore_broadcasts = \<span
class="number"\>1\</span\>

\<span class="preprocessor"\># Disable source packet routing\</span\>
net\<span class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.all\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.accept\</span\>\_source_route = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>6\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.all\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.accept\</span\>\_source_route = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.default\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.accept\</span\>\_source_route = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>6\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.default\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.accept\</span\>\_source_route = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\>

\<span class="preprocessor"\># Ignore send redirects\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.all\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.send\</span\>\_redirects = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.default\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.send\</span\>\_redirects = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\>

\<span class="preprocessor"\># Block SYN attacks\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.tcp\</span\>\_syncookies = \<span
class="number"\>1\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.tcp\</span\>\_max_syn_backlog = \<span
class="number"\>2048\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.tcp\</span\>\_synack_retries = \<span
class="number"\>2\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.tcp\</span\>\_syn_retries = \<span
class="number"\>5\</span\>

\<span class="preprocessor"\># Log Martians\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.all\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.log\</span\>\_martians = \<span
class="number"\>1\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.icmp\</span\>\_ignore_bogus_error_responses =
\<span class="number"\>1\</span\>

\<span class="preprocessor"\># Ignore ICMP redirects\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.all\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.accept\</span\>\_redirects = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>6\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.all\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.accept\</span\>\_redirects = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.default\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.accept\</span\>\_redirects = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>6\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.default\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.accept\</span\>\_redirects = \<span
class="number"\>0\</span\>

\<span class="preprocessor"\># Ignore Directed pings\</span\> net\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.ipv\</span\>4\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.icmp\</span\>\_echo_ignore_all = \<span
class="number"\>1\</span\> \</code\>

Add all this and reload these configs\<br /\> \<code class="haskell"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\> sysctl
-p \</code\>

\<a href="https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg#top"\>^top^\</a\>\<br /\>
\<h3\> Prevent IP spoofing\</h3\> Add or edit the following lines in
\<code style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>/etc/host.conf\</code\>:\<br /\>
\<code class="apache" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>order\</span\> bind,hosts nospoof \<span
class="literal"\>on\</span\> \</code\>

\<a href="https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg#top"\>^top^\</a\>\<br /\>
\<h3\> Secure shared memory\</h3\> Add this to your \<code
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>/etc/fstab\</code\> file:\<br /\> \<code
class="haskell" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span
class="title"\>tmpfs\</span\> /dev/shm tmpfs defaults,noexec,nosuid
\<span class="number"\>0\</span\> \<span class="number"\>0\</span\>
\</code\>

Mount it.\<br /\> \<code class="haskell" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\> mount -a \</code\>

\<a href="https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg#top"\>^top^\</a\>\<br /\>
\<h3\> IP tables\</h3\> Let's create a new IP tables files that we will
load in ip tables to complement what fail2ban has there already.\<br /\>
\<code class="avrasm" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo vim
/etc/iptables\<span class="preprocessor"\>.firewall\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.rules\</span\> \</code\>

Copy this, according to your own port settings:\<br /\> \<code
class="vhdl"\>\*filter

# Allow \<span class="keyword"\>all\</span\> loopback (lo0) traffic \<span class="keyword"\>and\</span\> drop \<span class="keyword"\>all\</span\> traffic \<span class="keyword"\>to\</span\> \<span class="number"\>127\</span\>/\<span class="number"\>8\</span\> that doesn't \<span class="keyword"\>use\</span\> lo0

-A INPUT -i lo -j ACCEPT -A INPUT ! -i lo -d \<span
class="number"\>127.0\</span\>\<span class="number"\>.0\</span\>\<span
class="number"\>.0\</span\>/\<span class="number"\>8\</span\> -j \<span
class="keyword"\>REJECT\</span\>

# Accept \<span class="keyword"\>all\</span\> established inbound connections

-A INPUT -m state \<span class="comment"\>--state ESTABLISHED,RELATED -j
ACCEPT\</span\>

# Allow \<span class="keyword"\>all\</span\> outbound traffic - you can modify this \<span class="keyword"\>to\</span\> only allow certain traffic

-A OUTPUT -j ACCEPT

# Allow HTTP \<span class="keyword"\>and\</span\> HTTPS connections from anywhere (the normal ports \<span class="keyword"\>for\</span\> websites \<span class="keyword"\>and\</span\> SSL).

-A INPUT -p tcp \<span class="comment"\>--dport 80 -j ACCEPT\</span\> -A
INPUT -p tcp \<span class="comment"\>--dport 443 -j ACCEPT\</span\>

# Allow ports \<span class="keyword"\>for\</span\> testing

-A INPUT -p tcp \<span class="comment"\>--dport 8080:8090 -j
ACCEPT\</span\>

# Allow ports \<span class="keyword"\>for\</span\> MOSH (mobile shell)

-A INPUT -p udp \<span class="comment"\>--dport 60000:61000 -j
ACCEPT\</span\>

# Allow SSH connections

# The -dport number should be the same \<span class="keyword"\>port\</span\> number you set \<span class="keyword"\>in\</span\> sshd_config

-A INPUT -p tcp -m state \<span class="comment"\>--state NEW --dport 22
-j ACCEPT\</span\>

# Allow ping

-A INPUT -p icmp -m icmp \<span class="comment"\>--icmp-type 8 -j
ACCEPT\</span\>

# Log iptables denied calls

-A INPUT -m limit \<span class="comment"\>--limit 5/min -j LOG
--log-prefix "iptables denied:" --log-level 7\</span\>

# \<span class="keyword"\>Reject\</span\> \<span class="keyword"\>all\</span\> other inbound - default deny unless explicitly allowed policy

-A INPUT -j \<span class="keyword"\>REJECT\</span\> -A FORWARD -j \<span
class="keyword"\>REJECT\</span\>

COMMIT \</code\>

Save the rules and prepare a network up script\<br /\> \<code
class="haskell" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span
class="title"\>sudo\</span\> iptables-restore &lt;
/etc/iptables.firewall.rules \<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\>
iptables -\<span class="label"\>L\</span\> \<span
class="title"\>sudo\</span\> vim /etc/network/\<span
class="keyword"\>if\</span\>-pre-up.d/firewall \</code\>

Copy this in the script you created\<br /\> \<code class="bash"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span class="shebang"\>#!/bin/sh\</span\>
/sbin/iptables-restore &lt; /etc/iptables.firewall.rules \</code\>

Make it executable\<br /\> \<code class="perl" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>sudo \<span class="keyword"\>chmod\</span\> +\<span
class="keyword"\>x\</span\> /etc/network/\<span
class="keyword"\>if\</span\>-pre-up.d/firewall \</code\>

This will make sure the IP tables are saved on a server restart. Note
that tcp ports \<code style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>8080\</code\> to
\<code style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>8090\</code\> are open for dev
purposes. You might want to remove those if you do not use them.\<br /\>
\<a href="https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg#top"\>^top^\</a\>\<br /\>
\<h3\> Setup fail2ban\</h3\> \<code class="avrasm" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>sudo apt-get install fail2ban sudo \<span
class="keyword"\>cp\</span\> /etc/fail2ban/jail\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\> /etc/fail2ban/jail\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.local\</span\> sudo vim /etc/fail2ban/jail\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.local\</span\> \</code\>

Add or edit these lines\<br /\> \<code class="ini"\>\<span
class="setting"\>destemail = \<span
class="value"\>admin@linodedomain.com\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>action = \<span
class="value"\>%(action_mwl)s\</span\>\</span\>

\<span class="title"\>\[ssh\]\</span\>

\<span class="setting"\>enabled = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>true\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>port = \<span class="value"\>ssh\</span\>\</span\>
\<span class="setting"\>filter = \<span
class="value"\>sshd\</span\>\</span\> \<span class="setting"\>logpath =
\<span class="value"\>/var/log/auth.log\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>maxretry = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="number"\>6\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>

\<span class="title"\>\[ssh-ddos\]\</span\>

\<span class="setting"\>enabled = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>true\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>port = \<span class="value"\>ssh\</span\>\</span\>
\<span class="setting"\>filter = \<span
class="value"\>sshd-ddos\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>logpath = \<span
class="value"\>/var/log/auth.log\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>maxretry = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="number"\>6\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \</code\>

Basically make sure ssh and ssh-dos are set to true, and change ssh port
if needed.\<br /\> \<code class="haskell" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\> service fail2ban restart
\</code\>

Note that fail2bans adds it's own rule to iptables on it's own at boot
time, no need to add them to our script.\<br /\> \<pre\>\<span
style="font-size: 14px;"\>&nbsp;\</span\>\</pre\> \<pre\>\<span
style="font-size: 14px;"\>&nbsp;\</span\>\</pre\> \<h2\> LAMP+\</h2\>
\<h3\> Postfix and gmail\</h3\> First let's start by configuring our
email server using gmail, because who runs their own mail server these
days ;)\<br /\> \<code class="actionscript" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>sudo apt-\<span class="keyword"\>get\</span\> install postfix
mailutils libsasl2-\<span class="number"\>2\</span\> ca-certificates
libsasl2-modules \</code\>

Choose internet site for the config, and enter any email, you'll change
it later.\<br /\> \<code class="avrasm" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>sudo vim /etc/postfix/main\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.cf\</span\> \</code\>

Add this at the end\<br /\> \<code class="ini" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>\<span class="setting"\>relayhost = \<span
class="value"\>\[smtp.gmail.com\]:\<span
class="number"\>587\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>smtp_sasl_auth_enable = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>yes\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>smtp_sasl_password_maps = \<span
class="value"\>hash:/etc/postfix/sasl_passwd\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>smtp_sasl_security_options = \<span
class="value"\>noanonymous\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>smtp_tls_CAfile = \<span
class="value"\>/etc/postfix/cacert.pem\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>smtp_use_tls = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>yes\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \</code\>

Create our password file\<br /\> \<code class="haskell"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>vim\</span\>
/etc/postfix/sasl_passwd \</code\>

And add following line:\<br /\> \<code class="avrasm" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>\[smtp\<span class="preprocessor"\>.gmail\</span\>\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.com\</span\>\]:\<span
class="number"\>587\</span\> USERNAME@gmail\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.com\</span\>:PASSWORD \</code\>

If you want to use your Google App's domain, please replace @gmail.com
with your @domain.com.\<br /\> Fix permission and update postfix config
to use sasl_passwd file:\<br /\> \<code class="haskell"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\> chmod
\<span class="number"\>400\</span\> /etc/postfix/sasl_passwd \<span
class="title"\>sudo\</span\> postmap /etc/postfix/sasl_passwd \</code\>

Next, validate certificates to avoid running into error. Just run
following command:\<br /\> \<code class="avrasm" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>cat /etc/ssl/certs/Thawte_Premium_Server_CA\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.pem\</span\> \| sudo tee -a
/etc/postfix/cacert\<span class="preprocessor"\>.pem\</span\> \</code\>

Finally, reload postfix config for changes to take effect:\<br /\>
\<code class="avrasm" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo /etc/init\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.d\</span\>/postfix reload \</code\>

If you have configured everything correctly, following command should
generate a test mail from your server to your mailbox.\<br /\> \<code
class="perl" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>echo \<span
class="string"\>"Test mail from postfix"\</span\> \| mail -\<span
class="keyword"\>s\</span\> \<span class="string"\>"Test
Postfix"\</span\> you\<span class="variable"\>@example&lt;/span\>.com
\</code\>

This whole section is pretty much a copy/paste from \<a
href="http://rtcamp.com/wordpress-nginx/tutorials/linux/ubuntu-postfix-gmail-smtp/"\>rtcamp.com\</a\>.
Credits!\<br /\> Delete the \<code style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>/etc/postfix/sasl_passwd file\</code\> you created. The \<code
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>postmap\</code\> command converted it,
delete this clear text file with your gmail password!\<br /\> Now
forward all root mails, edit \<code style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>/etc/aliases\</code\>\<br /\> \<code class="avrasm"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span class="label"\>root:\</span\>
username@gmail\<span class="preprocessor"\>.com\</span\> \</code\>

Then, rebuild aliases:\<br /\> \<code class="haskell" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>newaliases\</span\> \</code\>

\<a href="https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg#top"\>^top^\</a\>\<br /\>
\<h3\> Apache\</h3\> \<code class="actionscript" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>sudo apt-\<span class="keyword"\>get\</span\> install apache
\</code\>

Optimise apache2 for a Linode 1GB:\<br /\> \<code class="avrasm"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo vim /etc/apache2/apache2\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.conf\</span\> \</code\>

And make sure these settings match for this section:\<br /\> \<code
class="apache" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span
class="tag"\>\<ifmodule mpm_prefork_module=""\>\</ifmodule\>\</span\>
\<span class="keyword"\>StartServers\</span\> 2 \<span
class="keyword"\>MinSpareServers\</span\> 6 \<span
class="keyword"\>MaxSpareServers\</span\> 12 \<span
class="keyword"\>MaxClients\</span\> 30 \<span
class="keyword"\>MaxRequestsPerChild\</span\> 3000 \<span
class="tag"\>\</span\>\</code\>

Secure apache 2, open:\<br /\> \<code class="avrasm" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>sudo vim /etc/apache2/conf\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.d\</span\>/security \</code\>

Add or edit these lines:\<br /\> \<code class="apache"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>ServerTokens\</span\> Prod \<span
class="keyword"\>ServerSignature\</span\> \<span
class="literal"\>Off\</span\> \<span
class="keyword"\>TraceEnable\</span\> \<span
class="literal"\>Off\</span\> \<span class="keyword"\>Header\</span\>
unset ETag \<span class="keyword"\>FileETag\</span\> None \</code\>

Fix some modules and restart apache2:\<br /\> \<code class="haskell"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\> a2enmod
headers \<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\> a2dismod autoindex \<span
class="title"\>sudo\</span\> a2dismod status \<span
class="title"\>sudo\</span\> a2dismod cgi \<span
class="title"\>sudo\</span\> service apache2 restart \</code\>

We will come back to setting up virtual hosts later.\<br /\> \<a
href="https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg#top"\>^top^\</a\>\<br /\> \<h3\>
MySQL\</h3\> \<code class="vbscript" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo
apt-\<span class="keyword"\>get\</span\> install mysql-\<span
class="built_in"\>server\</span\> \</code\>

During the install enter the password you want for the MySQL root user.
Now secure the installation:\<br /\> \<code class="haskell"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\>
mysql_secure_installation \</code\>

Optimise MySQL for a Linode 1GB:\<br /\> \<code class="avrasm"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo vim /etc/mysql/my\<span
class="preprocessor"\>.cnf\</span\> \</code\>

Make sure the following values are set:\<br /\> \<code class="ini"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span class="setting"\>max_connections =
\<span class="value"\>\<span
class="number"\>75\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>key_buffer = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="number"\>32\</span\>M\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>max_allowed_packet = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="number"\>1\</span\>M\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>thread_stack = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="number"\>128\</span\>K\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>table_cache = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="number"\>32\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \</code\>

Restart MySQL:\<br /\> \<code class="haskell" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>\<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\> service mysql restart
\</code\>

Lets try to keep these sql databases in good shape:\<br /\> \<code
class="haskell" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span
class="title"\>sudo\</span\> crontab -e \</code\>

Add this line:\<br /\> \<code class="apache" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>@weekly mysqlcheck -o --\<span
class="keyword"\>user\</span\>=root --password=sqlrootpwd -A \</code\>

Now let's automate backups:\<br /\> \<code class="actionscript"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo apt-\<span
class="keyword"\>get\</span\> install automysqlbackup sudo vim
/etc/\<span class="keyword"\>default\</span\>/automysqlbackup \</code\>

Change \<code style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>BACKUPDIR="/home/\<your
username=""\>/sqlbackup/"\</your\>\</code\> and \<code
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>MAILADDR="admin@linodedomain.com"\</code\>
Also change \<code style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>DBNAMES\</code\> to
this:\<br /\> \<code class="parser3" style="overflow-y:
hidden;"\>DBNAMES=`mysql --defaults-file=/etc/mysql/debian.cnf --execute="SHOW DATABASES" | awk '{print &lt;span class="variable"&gt;$1}&lt;/span&gt;' | grep -v &lt;span class="keyword"&gt;^Database&lt;/span&gt;$ | grep -v &lt;span class="keyword"&gt;^mysql&lt;/span&gt;$ | grep -v &lt;span class="keyword"&gt;^information_schema&lt;/span&gt;$ | grep -v &lt;span class="keyword"&gt;^performance_schema&lt;/span&gt;$ | tr \\\r\\\n ,\`
\</code\>

This will prevent false positive errors. This was already set in my
Debian 7 distro.\<br /\> That's it, you will receive an email in case of
errors during the backup.\<br /\> \<a
href="https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg#top"\>^top^\</a\>\<br /\> \<h3\>
PHP\</h3\> \<code class="haskell" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span
class="title"\>sudo\</span\> apt-get install php5 php-pear php5-mysql
\<span class="title"\>sudo\</span\> service apache2 restart \</code\>

php5-suhosin was removed from Debian 7 and I am keeping the install bare
for now. Now let's optimise for a Linode 1GB and harden our php
install:\<br /\> \<code class="avrasm" style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>sudo
vim /etc/php5/apache2/php\<span class="preprocessor"\>.ini\</span\>
\</code\>

Make sure the following values are set:\<br /\> \<code class="ini"
style="overflow-y: hidden;"\>\<span class="setting"\>max_execution_time
= \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="number"\>30\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>memory_limit = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="number"\>128\</span\>M\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>error_reporting = \<span
class="value"\>E_COMPILE_ERROR\|E_RECOVERABLE_ERROR\|E_ERROR\|E_CORE_ERROR\</span\>\</span\>
\<span class="setting"\>display_errors = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>Off\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>log_errors = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>On\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>error_log = \<span
class="value"\>/var/log/php.log\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>register_globals = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>Off\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>disable_functions = \<span
class="value"\>exec,system,shell_exec,passthru (add those to existing
list)\</span\>\</span\> \<span class="setting"\>expose_php = \<span
class="value"\>\<span class="keyword"\>Off\</span\>\</span\>\</span\>
\<span class="setting"\>track_errors = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>Off\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \<span
class="setting"\>html_errors = \<span class="value"\>\<span
class="keyword"\>Off\</span\>\</span\>\</span\> \</code\>

Restart apache.\<br /\> \<br /\> \<br /\>
http://www.linuxquestions.org/questions/blog/rearden888-507430/howto-set-up-modsecurity-on-debian-7-35569/\<br
/\> \<br /\> \<h1 id="blog_title" style="font-size: 14pt; font-weight:
normal; margin: 0px;"\> HOWTO: Set up Modsecurity on Debian 7

\</h1\> \<div class="smallfont shade"\> \<span class="shade"\>Posted
06-10-2013 at 07:30 PM by\</span\> \<a
href="http://www.linuxquestions.org/questions/blog/rearden888-507430/"\>Rearden888\</a\>

    &lt;br /&gt;

\<span class="shade"\>Updated 06-10-2013 at 07:43 PM by\</span\> \<a
href="http://www.linuxquestions.org/questions/blog/rearden888-507430/"\>Rearden888\</a\>
\<span class="shade"\>(typos)\</span\>

\</div\> \<div class="smallfont" id="blogtagcontainer_35569"\> \<span
class="shade"\>Tags\</span\> \<span id="blogtaglist_35569"\>\<a
href="http://www.linuxquestions.org/questions/blog.php?tag=apache&amp;u=507430"
rel="nofollow"\>apache\</a\>, \<a
href="http://www.linuxquestions.org/questions/blog.php?tag=modsecurity&amp;u=507430"
rel="nofollow"\>modsecurity\</a\>, \<a
href="http://www.linuxquestions.org/questions/blog.php?tag=security&amp;u=507430"
rel="nofollow"\>security\</a\>, \<a
href="http://www.linuxquestions.org/questions/blog.php?tag=server&amp;u=507430"
rel="nofollow"\>server\</a\>\</span\> \</div\> \<hr size="1"
style="background-color: white; color: white; margin-bottom: 10px;" /\>
There are many places online that explain how to install and perform
initial set up for modsecurity on Apache. However, I haven't found
anywhere that shows how to do it with the standard Debian packages and
that respects the normal apt update process. The caveat here is that
like a lot of standard Debian packages, the packages included in wheezy
lag upstream by a few versions. This is obviously something to consider,
especially when dealing with security related software. If you're like
me, and prefer having all package maintenance bound up in apt,
particularly on production servers, so it all happens automatically,
this is the trade-off required by Debian. Throughout this article, I
will assume you're running as root, just to save having to type "sudo"
82 times.\
Just realize that if you're running as a normal user, most of these
commands require sudo.\<br /\> \<br /\> 1. Install and Activate the
software:\<br /\> \<br /\> Run the following commands to install the xml
and other supporting libraries required:\<br /\> \<div style="clear:
both; margin-top: 5px; margin: 20px;"\> \<div class="smallfont"
style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\> Code:\</div\> \<pre class="alt2" dir="ltr"
style="border: 1px inset; height: 50px; margin-right: -99999px; margin:
0px; overflow: auto; padding: 3px; text-align: left; width:
98%;"\>apt-get install libxml2 libxml2-dev libxml2-utils apt-get install
libaprutil1 libaprutil1-dev\</pre\> \</div\> On my server, the second
command also installed a lot of extra dependencies.\<br /\> \<br /\>
You're ready to install modsecurity itself. Run the following command,
and apt will install and activate modsecurity. Realize this will also
restart your apache server.\<br /\> \<div style="clear: both;
margin-top: 5px; margin: 20px;"\> \<div class="smallfont"
style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\> Code:\</div\> \<pre class="alt2" dir="ltr"
style="border: 1px inset; height: 34px; margin-right: -99999px; margin:
0px; overflow: auto; padding: 3px; text-align: left; width:
98%;"\>apt-get install libapache-mod-security\</pre\> \</div\> In order
to make full use of modsec, the "headers" apache module is required as
well, so activate it now:\<br /\> \<div style="clear: both; margin-top:
5px; margin: 20px;"\> \<div class="smallfont" style="margin-bottom:
2px;"\> Code:\</div\> \<pre class="alt2" dir="ltr" style="border: 1px
inset; height: 50px; margin-right: -99999px; margin: 0px; overflow:
auto; padding: 3px; text-align: left; width: 98%;"\>a2enmod headers
service apache2 restart\</pre\> \</div\> 2. Examine Apache config:\<br
/\> \<br /\> Before we dive in to editing config files, lets first talk
about how the configuration is organized by default in Debian. Many
online tutorials instruct you at this point to edit the apache config
file manually to activate, configure, and load modsecurity. We don't
need to do this in our case, since Debian provides it's own apache
control utilities and files which take care of it (a2enmod,
specifically, in this case). If you inspect the default Debian provided
config file at /etc/apache2/mods-enabled/\<span
class="skimlinks-unlinked"\>mod-security.conf\</span\> you'll see
something like this:\<br /\> \<div style="clear: both; margin-top: 5px;
margin: 20px;"\> \<div class="smallfont" style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\>
Code:\</div\> \<pre class="alt2" dir="ltr" style="border: 1px inset;
height: 178px; margin-right: -99999px; margin: 0px; overflow: auto;
padding: 3px; text-align: left; width: 98%;"\>\<ifmodule
security2_module=""\> \# Default Debian dir for modsecurity's persistent
data SecDataDir /var/cache/modsecurity

        # Include all the *.conf files in /etc/modsecurity.
        # Keeping your local configuration in that directory
        # will allow for an easy upgrade of THIS file and
        # make your life easier
        Include "/etc/modsecurity/*.conf"

\</ifmodule\>\</pre\> \</div\> The important part of this is the
"Include"/etc/modsecurity/*.conf"" line. The /etc/modsecurity folder
will be your primary place to set up and configure modsecurity. This
configuration file, combined with \<span
class="skimlinks-unlinked"\>mod-security.load\</span\>, do everything
required to pull the modsecurity module into your apache server. We
don't need to hand-modify any of apache's configuration, which is nice.
\<br /\> \<br /\> 3. Activate and Load modsecurity-specific
configuration:\<br /\> \<br /\> At this point, modsecurity is loaded
into the apache server, but isn't doing anything. We want it to start
filtering requests, so we need to activate the modsecurity-specific
configuration and load some rules.\<br /\> Now, the first step is to
enable the "recommended" modsecurity configuration file:\<br /\> \<br
/\> \<div style="clear: both; margin-top: 5px; margin: 20px;"\> \<div
class="smallfont" style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\> Code:\</div\> \<pre
class="alt2" dir="ltr" style="border: 1px inset; height: 50px;
margin-right: -99999px; margin: 0px; overflow: auto; padding: 3px;
text-align: left; width: 98%;"\>cd /etc/modsecurity mv \<span
class="skimlinks-unlinked"\>modsecurity.conf-recommended\</span\> \<span
class="skimlinks-unlinked"\>modsecurity.conf\</span\>\</pre\> \</div\>
By default, this file enables modsecurity in an "examine only" mode. In
order to make full use of the module, we have to make a few changes. Use
your favorite text editor to open \<span
class="skimlinks-unlinked"\>modsecurity.conf\</span\> and make the
following change:\<br /\> \<div style="clear: both; margin-top: 5px;
margin: 20px;"\> \<div class="smallfont" style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\>
Code:\</div\> \<pre class="alt2" dir="ltr" style="border: 1px inset;
height: 34px; margin-right: -99999px; margin: 0px; overflow: auto;
padding: 3px; text-align: left; width: 98%;"\>SecRuleEngine On\</pre\>
\</div\> This allows modsecurity to block requests based on its rules,
which we'll activate in a moment. Some other settings in this file that
are useful to know about are the debug controls, if you're
troubleshooting. \<br /\> \<br /\> \<div style="clear: both; margin-top:
5px; margin: 20px;"\> \<div class="smallfont" style="margin-bottom:
2px;"\> Code:\</div\> \<pre class="alt2" dir="ltr" style="border: 1px
inset; height: 50px; margin-right: -99999px; margin: 0px; overflow:
auto; padding: 3px; text-align: left; width: 98%;"\>#SecDebugLog
/opt/modsecurity/var/log/\<span
class="skimlinks-unlinked"\>debug.log\</span\> #SecDebugLogLevel
3\</pre\> \</div\> Also, this controls how much information is stored in
modsecurity's "audit log." This tracks attacks being made on your
server. By default, it stores everything, which can get huge quickly if
you have even a moderately busy server.\<br /\> \<br /\> \<div
style="clear: both; margin-top: 5px; margin: 20px;"\> \<div
class="smallfont" style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\> Code:\</div\> \<pre
class="alt2" dir="ltr" style="border: 1px inset; height: 34px;
margin-right: -99999px; margin: 0px; overflow: auto; padding: 3px;
text-align: left; width: 98%;"\>SecAuditLogParts ABIJDEFHZ\</pre\>
\</div\> \<br /\> 4. Activate modsecurity rules:\<br /\> \<br /\>
Modsecurity does its work by using rules which define the patterns it
uses to recognize when your website is being probed or attacked. When we
installed the modsecurity base package, apt also helpfully installed the
modsecurity-crs package, which contains the free core rule set.\
Ideally, we would want to go get the most recent version of these rules
from \<span class="skimlinks-unlinked"\>modsecurity.org\</span\>.
However, because of the package lag inherent in Debian, we can't. Core
rule sets newer than the version included with wheezy (ver 2.2.5-2)
require at least version 2.7 of the modsecurity plugin, which isn't
available in default wheezy. So, we can't really get the newest rules
without having to manually recompile modsecurity. Since I like to keep
my production servers as close to vanilla as possible and it's often not
a great idea to compile software on a production machine, we'll continue
with the default wheezy packages and file locations.\<br /\> \<br /\>
The crs (core rule set) is installed in /usr/share/modsecurity-crs by
default. This directory contains an "activated_rules" directory which we
won't be using since we already have a de-facto "activated rules"
directory: /etc/modsecurity \<br /\> \<br /\> The preferred method to
activate rules is by symlinking from the actual config and rule files
into the config directory. This allows the package manager to update the
files as necessary, without requiring the administrator to manually copy
or edit files after an update. Some other tutorials recommend copying
the /usr/share/modsecurity directory into /etc/modsecurity, however this
also requires manual action after an update, and it's not necessary with
the symlink technique.\<br /\> \<br /\> We'll be making links from the
/usr/share/modsecurity location into /etc/modsecurity to activate our
desired configuration. First, we link to the main crs config file:\<br
/\> \<br /\> \<div style="clear: both; margin-top: 5px; margin: 20px;"\>
\<div class="smallfont" style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\> Code:\</div\>
\<pre class="alt2" dir="ltr" style="border: 1px inset; height: 34px;
margin-right: -99999px; margin: 0px; overflow: auto; padding: 3px;
text-align: left; width: 98%;"\>ln -s
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/modsecurity_crs_10_setup.conf
/etc/modsecurity/modsecurity_crs_10_setup.conf\</pre\> \</div\> This
file provides some basic configuration directives for the crs.\<br /\>
\<br /\> Now, we'll link each rule file in the base_rules and
optional_rules directories using some quick shell magic:\<br /\> \<br
/\> \<div style="clear: both; margin-top: 5px; margin: 20px;"\> \<div
class="smallfont" style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\> Code:\</div\> \<pre
class="alt2" dir="ltr" style="border: 1px inset; height: 82px;
margin-right: -99999px; margin: 0px; overflow: auto; padding: 3px;
text-align: left; width: 98%;"\>cd /usr/share/modsecurity-crs/base_rules
for f in * ; do sudo ln -s
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/base_rules/$f /etc/modsecurity/$f ; done cd
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/optional_rules for f in \* ; do sudo ln -s
/usr/share/modsecurity-crs/optional_rules/$f /etc/modsecurity/$f ;
done\</pre\> \</div\> With that done, there's one more edit to check if
modsecurity blocking works as expected. Open the /etc/modsecurity/\<span
class="skimlinks-unlinked"\>modsecurity.conf\</span\> file and add the
following lines at the end (this is from the free, modsecurity pdf book,
link provided below)\<br /\> \<br /\> \<div style="clear: both;
margin-top: 5px; margin: 20px;"\> \<div class="smallfont"
style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\> Code:\</div\> \<pre class="alt2" dir="ltr"
style="border: 1px inset; height: 50px; margin-right: -99999px; margin:
0px; overflow: auto; padding: 3px; text-align: left; width:
98%;"\>SecRule ARGS "MY_UNIQUE_TEST_STRING"\
"phase:1,log,deny,status:503"\</pre\> \</div\> That's it. Run\<br /\>
\<div style="clear: both; margin-top: 5px; margin: 20px;"\> \<div
class="smallfont" style="margin-bottom: 2px;"\> Code:\</div\> \<pre
class="alt2" dir="ltr" style="border: 1px inset; height: 34px;
margin-right: -99999px; margin: 0px; overflow: auto; padding: 3px;
text-align: left; width: 98%;"\>sudo service apache2 restart\</pre\>
\</div\> Assuming it restarts cleanly, you're done!\<br /\> \<br /\> To
verify your installation, open a browser and attempt to access your site
like this:\<br /\> \<a
href="http://www.example.com/?test=MY_UNIQUE_TEST_STRING" rel="nofollow"
target="\_blank"\>http://www.example.com/?test=MY_UNIQUE_TEST_STRING\</a\>\<br
/\> \<br /\> You should see a 503 "Service Temporarily Unavailable"
message from the server. You can also examine your servers modsec audit
log file (default location /var/log/apache2/\<span
class="skimlinks-unlinked"\>modsec_audit.log\</span\>) and search for
that string. You will find the full transcript of the communication
between your browser and server. Depending on the amount of traffic your
site receives, you should monitor the size of this file for a while
after installing modsec and probably configure your log rotating utility
to know about it and rotate the file periodically. \<br /\> \<br /\>
That's it. You've set up modsecurity on a standard Debian 7 in such a
way that it will update automatically and work with apt updates. \<br
/\> \<br /\> Please feel free to ask questions or post mistakes in the
comments.\<br /\> \<br /\> Further reading:\<br /\> Modsec Getting
started Book:\<br /\> \<a
href="https://www.feistyduck.com/books/modsecurity-handbook/modsecurity-handbook-getting-started-may-2012.pdf"
rel="nofollow"
target="\_blank"\>https://www.feistyduck.com/books/mod...d-may-2012.pdf\</a\>\<br
/\> \<br /\> Modsec Site:\<br /\> \<a href="http://www.modsecurity.org/"
rel="nofollow" target="\_blank"\>http://www.modsecurity.org/\</a\>\<br
/\> \<br /\>
http://www.unixmen.com/install-apache2-fastcgi-ubuntu-server-14-0413-10/
\<br /\> \<pre\>\<span style="font-size: 14px;"\>&nbsp;\</span\>\</pre\>
\<pre\>\<span style="font-size: 14px;"\>https://coderwall.com/p/zxffsg
\</span\>\</pre\>

```{=html}
<title type="text">
```
```{=html}
</title>
```
`<content type='html'>`{=html}\<div id="r1PostCPBlock"
style="background-color: white; border: medium none; left: -99999px;
overflow: hidden; position: absolute; text-align: left; text-decoration:
none;"\> On the install of Ubuntu this evening, instead of letting
Ubuntu partition the drive, I decided to do it manually. \<br /\> To do
this I needed to learn enough about the partitioning process to be able
to do it myself.\<br /\> I found one really good article on the subject
here:\<br /\> \<span style="color: black;"\>\<a
href="http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1986743"
target="\_blank"\>http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1986743\</a\>\</span\>\<br
/\> The basic premise of the above article is to use LVM, and create
lots of separate partitions, using LVM (Logical Volume Manager). The
instructions on this page outline using LVM to partition the drive. In
another article, I will show another method, which does NOT use LVM (ie
a less complex approach).\<br /\> The author of that article was gearing
his server for a slightly different application, so I came up with my
own plan for how the hard drive on my server was going to be laid out.
Note: I am using quantity 2 - 2 2TB drives, setup in a hardware RAID
configuration (mirrored for auto backup). Here's the basic layout of the
partitions in this design:\<br /\> Outside the LVM (Logical Volume
Manager):\<br /\> \<b\>boot - 200 MB - This will remain static in size.
It is also the only space residing outside the Logical Volume Manager
(LVM)\</b\>\<br /\> Inside the LVM I have:\<br /\> \<b\>root - 20 GB -
Operating system and everything else which should remain fairly
static.\<br /\>swap - 8G (2 \* amount of RAM) - This will most likely
remain static in size. However, if amount of RAM is adjusted, this can
be adjusted as well.\<br /\>var - 500GB - This is the
website/database/log storage and will continue to grow over
time.\</b\>\<br /\> These are the step by step instructions for the
settings I entered:\<br /\> \<ol\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Manual\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>SCSI3 (0,0,0) (sda) - 8.6 GB VMware
Virtual disk\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Yes\</i\> to create
new empty partition table, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>pri/log FREE
SPACE\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Create a new
partition\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>200 MB\</b\>, {ENTER}
(NOTE: This will be the /boot partition)\</li\> \<li\>Select
\<i\>Primary\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Beginning\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Use as: Ext4 journaling file
system\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Ext2 file system\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Mount point: /\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>/boot - static files of the boot loader\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Bootable flag: off\</i\> {ENTER} (NOTE:
This toggles it on)\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Done setting up the
partition\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Configure the Logical
Volume Manager\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Yes\</i\> to write
change to disks and configure LVM, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select
\<i\>Create volume group\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>LVG\</b\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>/dev/sda FREE SPACE\</i\>, {SPACEBAR},
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Yes\</i\> to write change to disks and
configure LVM, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Create logical
volume\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>LVG (8384MB)\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>swap\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type
\<b\>8G\</b\> {ENTER} (NOTE: This is double the amount of RAM)\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>Create logical volume\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>LVG (6387MB)\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type
\<b\>root\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>20G\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>Create logical volume\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>LVG (6387MB)\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type
\<b\>var\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>500G\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>Finish\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \</ol\> Now that we've
created the Volume Groups, we need to go back in and tell the installer
which Linux partitions will be associated/mounted under the VGs created
above:\<br /\> \<ol\> \<li\>Select \<i\>#1 2.0 GB\</i\> directly under
\<i\>LVM VG LVG, LV swap\</i\>, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Use as:
do not use\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>swap area\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Done setting up the partition\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>#1 20.0 GB\</i\> directly under
\<i\>LVM VG LVG, LV root\</i\>, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Use as:
do not use\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Ext4 journaling file
system\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Mount point: none\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>/ - the root file system\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Done setting up the partition\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>#1 \</i\>directly under \<i\>LVM VG
LVG, LV var\</i\>, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Use as: do not
use\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Ext4 journaling file
system\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Mount point: none\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>/var\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select
\<i\>Label: none\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>var\</b\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Done setting up the partition\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Finish partitioning and write changes
to disk\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Yes\</i\> to write
changes to disk, {ENTER}\</li\> \</ol\> \<br /\> Read more at \<a
href="http://www.designervisuals.com/Manual_Partitioning_of_Ubuntu_Web_Server_using_LVM.html#EZgmyW2XpFh2KGJY.99"\>http://www.designervisuals.com/Manual_Partitioning_of_Ubuntu_Web_Server_using_LVM.html#EZgmyW2XpFh2KGJY.99\</a\>\</div\>
\<div id="r1PostCPBlock" style="background-color: white; border: medium
none; left: -99999px; overflow: hidden; position: absolute; text-align:
left; text-decoration: none;"\> Outside the LVM (Logical Volume
Manager):\<br /\> \<b\>boot - 200 MB - This will remain static in size.
It is also the only space residing outside the Logical Volume Manager
(LVM)\</b\>\<br /\> Inside the LVM I have:\<br /\> \<b\>root - 20 GB -
Operating system and everything else which should remain fairly
static.\<br /\>swap - 8G (2 \* amount of RAM) - This will most likely
remain static in size. However, if amount of RAM is adjusted, this can
be adjusted as well.\<br /\>var - 500GB - This is the
website/database/log storage and will continue to grow over
time.\</b\>\<br /\> These are the step by step instructions for the
settings I entered:\<br /\> \<ol\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Manual\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>SCSI3 (0,0,0) (sda) - 8.6 GB VMware
Virtual disk\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Yes\</i\> to create
new empty partition table, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>pri/log FREE
SPACE\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Create a new
partition\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>200 MB\</b\>, {ENTER}
(NOTE: This will be the /boot partition)\</li\> \<li\>Select
\<i\>Primary\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Beginning\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Use as: Ext4 journaling file
system\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Ext2 file system\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Mount point: /\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>/boot - static files of the boot loader\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Bootable flag: off\</i\> {ENTER} (NOTE:
This toggles it on)\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Done setting up the
partition\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Configure the Logical
Volume Manager\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Yes\</i\> to write
change to disks and configure LVM, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select
\<i\>Create volume group\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>LVG\</b\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>/dev/sda FREE SPACE\</i\>, {SPACEBAR},
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Yes\</i\> to write change to disks and
configure LVM, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Create logical
volume\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>LVG (8384MB)\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>swap\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type
\<b\>8G\</b\> {ENTER} (NOTE: This is double the amount of RAM)\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>Create logical volume\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>LVG (6387MB)\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type
\<b\>root\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>20G\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>Create logical volume\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>LVG (6387MB)\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type
\<b\>var\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>500G\</b\> {ENTER}\</li\>
\<li\>Select \<i\>Finish\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \</ol\> Now that we've
created the Volume Groups, we need to go back in and tell the installer
which Linux partitions will be associated/mounted under the VGs created
above:\<br /\> \<ol\> \<li\>Select \<i\>#1 2.0 GB\</i\> directly under
\<i\>LVM VG LVG, LV swap\</i\>, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Use as:
do not use\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>swap area\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Done setting up the partition\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>#1 20.0 GB\</i\> directly under
\<i\>LVM VG LVG, LV root\</i\>, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Use as:
do not use\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Ext4 journaling file
system\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Mount point: none\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>/ - the root file system\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Done setting up the partition\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>#1 \</i\>directly under \<i\>LVM VG
LVG, LV var\</i\>, {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Use as: do not
use\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Ext4 journaling file
system\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Mount point: none\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>/var\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select
\<i\>Label: none\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Type \<b\>var\</b\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Done setting up the partition\</i\>
{ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Finish partitioning and write changes
to disk\</i\> {ENTER}\</li\> \<li\>Select \<i\>Yes\</i\> to write
changes to disk, {ENTER}\</li\> \</ol\> \<br /\> Read more at \<a
href="http://www.designervisuals.com/Manual_Partitioning_of_Ubuntu_Web_Server_using_LVM.html#EZgmyW2XpFh2KGJY.99"\>http://www.designervisuals.com/Manual_Partitioning_of_Ubuntu_Web_Server_using_LVM.html#EZgmyW2XpFh2KGJY.99\</a\>\</div\>

http://downloads.mariadb.org/mariadb/repositories/`\ndeb `{=tex}http://ftp.osuosl.org/pub/mariadb/repo/5.5/ubuntu

PLUGIN BAGI MENGGUNAKAN CCCAM AMIKO ALIEN SHD 8900 / Salah Satu Cara
Setup Cline Firmware Asal SPARK
```{=html}
</title>
```
`<content type='html'>`{=html}\<div style="text-align: justify;"\>
\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\> 1. Download Plugin \<a
href="http://www.4shared.com/rar/fUcb8f-9/plugin.html"\>KLIK SINI\</a\>
dan Extract (File ini Mengandungi Plugin CCcam214,e2upgrade, mcas,
mgcamd, oscamd)\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\> 2. Buka
folder file tersebut plugin/var/key/ dan edit CCcam.cfg add account\<b\>
C: someserver.somedomain 12000 user1 pass1\</b\> ATAU Copy Paste file
CCcam.cfg anda dalam directory tsb\</div\> \<div style="text-align:
justify;"\> 3. Copy folder plugin(jangan ubah nama "plugin" ) ke
pendrive fat32 dan masukkan ke usb box AMIKO dan tunggu mesej keluar
automatic tanya comfirmation utk upgrade tekan YES\</div\> \<div
style="text-align: justify;"\> 4. Pergi ke MENU&gt;PLUGIN dan start
CCcam Plugin\</div\> \<div style="text-align: justify;"\> 5. Restart
&gt; Cline running\<br /\> \<br /\>\</div\>
`</content>`{=html}`<link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://lonurhazve.blogspot.com/2012/10/plugin-bagi-menggunakan-cccam-amiko.html#comment-form' title='0 Comments'/>`{=html}`<link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/5018747636464774102'/>`{=html}`<link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/5018747636464774102'/>`{=html}`<author>`{=html}`<name>`{=html}lonurhazve`</name>`{=html}`<uri>`{=html}https://www.blogger.com/profile/16306879527733710247`</uri>`{=html}`<email>`{=html}noreply@blogger.com`</email>`{=html}`<gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='35' height='35' src='//www.blogger.com/img/blogger_logo_round_35.png'/>`{=html}`</author>`{=html}`<thr:total>`{=html}0`</thr:total>`{=html}`</entry>`{=html}`<entry>`{=html}`<id>`{=html}tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-702950587710156521.post-9217303364554843347`</id>`{=html}`<published>`{=html}2012-10-02T15:44:00.000+08:00`</published>`{=html}`<updated>`{=html}2012-10-02T15:44:03.439+08:00`</updated>`{=html}`<app:control xmlns:app='http://purl.org/atom/app#'>`{=html}`<app:draft>`{=html}yes`</app:draft>`{=html}`</app:control>`{=html}`<category scheme='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#kind' term='http://schemas.google.com/blogger/2008/kind#post'/>`{=html}
```{=html}
<title type="text">
```
```{=html}
</title>
```
`<content type='html'>`{=html}oud.gmc.to\<br /\> D.OPENBOXFAN.COM\<br
/\> \<br /\> \<br /\> File WebZeal_v2.7su_20120323.mnt di FlashDisk\<br
/\> - Menu&nbsp; --&gt; Storage Manager&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &gt;&gt;&gt;
Current Device&nbsp; --&gt; File Mount Drive\<br /\> - Mount file name
--&gt; WebZeal_v2.7su_20120323.mnt --&gt; connect&nbsp; --&gt; Ok\<br
/\> - Plugin --&gt; Webzeal --&gt; Start

Time For MariaDB, Not Mysql Anymore
```{=html}
</title>
```
`<content type='html'>`{=html}\<code\>\</code\>\<br /\>
\<u\>\<code\>\<b\>Installation Mysql Server On Ubuntu 10.04 LTS ( Lucid
) Server\</b\> \</code\>\</u\>\<br /\> \<br /\> \<code\>\</code\>\<br
/\> \<code\>\<i\>( On root permission or sudo )\</i\> \</code\>\<br /\>
\<br /\> \<br /\> \<code\>\</code\>\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<b\>\<u\>\<code\>Langkah 1 : \</code\>\</u\>\</b\>\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<code\>Masukkan keyserver to keyserver.ubuntu.com\</code\>\<br /\>
\<code\>&nbsp;\</code\>\<br /\> \<code\>apt-key adv --recv-keys
--keyserver keyserver.ubuntu.com 1BB943DB\</code\>\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<u\>\<b\>\<code\>Langkah 2 :\</code\>\</b\>\</u\>\<br /\> \<code\>Buat
repository baru sebagaiamana berikut:\</code\>\<br /\>
\<code\>&nbsp;\</code\>\<br /\> \<code\>vi
/etc/apt/sources.list.d/mariadb.list\</code\>\<code\> \</code\>\<br /\>
\<br /\> \<code\>\</code\>\<br /\> \<u\>\<b\>\<code\>Langkah 3 :
\</code\>\</b\>\</u\>\<br /\> \<code\>Masukkan repo berikut dalam fail
mariadb.list dan save: \</code\>\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<code\>\</code\>\<code\>deb
http://mirror2.hs-esslingen.de/mariadb/repo/5.3/ubuntu lucid main\<br
/\>deb-src http://mirror2.hs-esslingen.de/mariadb/repo/5.3/ubuntu lucid
main\</code\>\<br /\> \<code\>\</code\>\<br /\> \<br /\>
\<u\>\<b\>\<code\>Langkah 4 :\</code\>\</b\>\</u\>\<br /\>
\<code\>Upadate dan Install guna apt-get :\</code\>\<br /\>
\<code\>\</code\>\<b\>\<code\>\<br /\>\</code\>\</b\>\<br /\>
\<code\>\</code\>\<code\>sudo apt-get
update\</code\>\<code\>&nbsp;\</code\>\<br /\> \<code\>sudo apt-get
install mariadb-server mariadb-client\</code\>\<br /\> \<code\>\<br
/\>\</code\>\<br /\> \<div class="separator" style="clear: both;
text-align: center;"\> \<a
href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgN1kuwPGkOfeXahdX28-7zRpOe-QOdpgyeYFSDHLNwULq8RCDdfuy-faODwoySEUZszS-9RX7J74pES1YKD9cOqIwRLrwrJt3XqOurkNIBMY1lEu9dwDOqsaFYWVpSD3qWqmsuwiUzBg/s1600/mdbinstall.jpg"
imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em;
margin-right: 1em;"\>\<img border="0" height="298"
src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgN1kuwPGkOfeXahdX28-7zRpOe-QOdpgyeYFSDHLNwULq8RCDdfuy-faODwoySEUZszS-9RX7J74pES1YKD9cOqIwRLrwrJt3XqOurkNIBMY1lEu9dwDOqsaFYWVpSD3qWqmsuwiUzBg/s640/mdbinstall.jpg"
width="640" /\>\</a\>\</div\> \<code\>\<br
/\>\</code\>`</content>`{=html}`<link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/4130696902793916741'/>`{=html}`<link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/702950587710156521/posts/default/4130696902793916741'/>`{=html}`<author>`{=html}`<name>`{=html}lonurhazve`</name>`{=html}`<uri>`{=html}https://www.blogger.com/profile/16306879527733710247`</uri>`{=html}`<email>`{=html}noreply@blogger.com`</email>`{=html}`<gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='35' height='35' src='//www.blogger.com/img/blogger_logo_round_35.png'/>`{=html}`</author>`{=html}`<media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgN1kuwPGkOfeXahdX28-7zRpOe-QOdpgyeYFSDHLNwULq8RCDdfuy-faODwoySEUZszS-9RX7J74pES1YKD9cOqIwRLrwrJt3XqOurkNIBMY1lEu9dwDOqsaFYWVpSD3qWqmsuwiUzBg/s72-c/mdbinstall.jpg' height='72' width='72'/>`{=html}`<thr:total>`{=html}0`</thr:total>`{=html}`</entry>`{=html}`<entry>`{=html}`<id>`{=html}tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-702950587710156521.post-7473896634970085200`</id>`{=html}`<published>`{=html}2012-03-14T00:26:00.001+08:00`</published>`{=html}`<updated>`{=html}2012-03-14T00:32:14.966+08:00`</updated>`{=html}`<category scheme='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#kind' term='http://schemas.google.com/blogger/2008/kind#post'/>`{=html}`<category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='life as IT workers'/>`{=html}
